The Two Categories of Agent Contracts in Hanafi Law
Explaining the principle of contract classification in agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of agency contract classification and apply it to identify whether rights attach to the agent or principal.

Core Idea
Rights attach to the agent when he attributes the contract to himself; to the principal when he attributes to the principal.

This lesson introduces a foundational rule (ḍābiṭah) in Hanafi law of agency (wakālah). The rule distinguishes two types of contracts that an agent (wakīl) concludes: those he attributes to himself and those he attributes to his principal (muwakkil). Understanding this classification is essential for determining who bears the rights and obligations arising from the agent's actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of contracts by attribution
Read the passage and note that contracts are divided into two groups based on whom the agent attributes the contract to: himself or the principal.
2
Recognize the parameter (ḍābiṭah)
The parameter is: every contract that the agent validly attributes to himself has its rights pertain to the agent; every contract he must attribute to the principal has its rights pertain to the principal.
The key is whether the agent can validly attribute the contract to himself and be independent of the principal's attribution.
3
Apply the rule to example contracts
Apply the rule: sale and lease are attributed to the agent, so the agent is liable. Marriage and khul' are attributed to the principal, so the principal is liable.
The practical implication is that the agent of the husband cannot be sued for dower; the agent of the wife cannot be forced to hand her over.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كُلَّ عَقْدٍ يُضِيفَهُ الْوَكِيلُ إِلَى نَفْسِهِ فَحُقُوقُهُ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْوَكِيلِ وَمَا هُوَ عَلَى الْعَكْسِ فَحُقُوقُهُ تَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْمُؤكّلِ .
ترجمہ: ہر وہ عقد جس کی نسبت وکیل اپنی طرف کرتا ہے اس کے حقوق وکیل سے متعلق ہوں گے اور جو اس کے برعکس ہو تو اس کے حقوق موکل کے ساتھ متعلق ہوں گے۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ہر ایسا عقد جس کی اضافت وقت عقد میں وکیل اپنی طرف کرے اور اس کا منسوب کرنا درست بھی ہو، مثلاً بیع وشراء اور اجارہ وغیرہ ، تو اس عقد کے تمام حقوق مثلاً بیع کا حوالہ کرنا ہشمن وصول کرنا وغیرہ وکیل سے وابستہ ہوں گے، اور ہر وہ عقد جس کی نسبت عقد کے وقت وکیل اپنے مؤکل کی طرف کرے، مثلاً نکاح، طلاق وغیرہ، تو اس عقد کے حقوق موکل سے وابستہ ہوں گے، مثلاً مہر کا مطالبہ عورت اپنے شوہر موکل سے کرے گی نہ کہ وکیل سے۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ نتلار ہے ہیں کہ وکیل با موج وکیل بالشراء میں حقوق وکیل کے ساتھ متعلق ہوں گے، یعنی مبیع سپرد کر نا ہشمن ادا کر کے مبیع وصول کرنا وکیل کی ذمہ داری ہوگی مؤکل کی نہیں ، کیونکہ ان میں وکیل عقد کی نسبت اپنی طرف کرتا ہے اور ہر وہ عقد جس میں وکیل نسبت اپنی طرف کرے اور نسبت کرنا درست بھی ہو تو اس عقد کے حقوق عِنْدَنَا غَيْرُ مَضْمُونَةٍ بِالْإِتلافِ لِأَنَّ التَّمِينَ يَقْتَضِي الْمُمَاثَلَةَ بِالنَّصِّ عَلَى مَا عُرِفَ، وَلَا مُمَاثَلَةَ بَيْنَ الْعَيْنِ وَالْمَنْفَعَةِ. (العناية: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج- ص۴۸۷) ولا مماثلة بين العين والمنفعة التى هى العوض، أعنى منفعة البضع، فلا يجب الضمان كما في إتلاف سائر منافع المغصوب، حيث لا يجب الضمان عندنا خلافا للشافعي (البناية : كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج ۶ ص ۲۰۲) الهداية كتاب الوكالة، ج ۳ ص ۱۸۷ ، ۱۸۸

الْعُقُودُ الَّتِي يَعْقِدُهَا الْوُكَلاءُ عَلَى ضَرْبَيْنِ : ضَرْبٌ يَتَعَلَّقُ حُقُوقُهُ بِالْوَكِيل، وَآخَرُ بِالْمُوَكَّلِ. فَضَابِطَةُ الْأَوَّلِ كُلُّ عَقْدِ يُضِيفُهُ الْوَكِيلُ إِلَى نَفْسِهِ كَالْبَيْعِ وَالْإِجَارَةِ فَحُقُوقُهُ تَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْوَكِيلِ ... كُلُّ عَقْدٍ يُضِيفُهُ الْوَكِيلُ إِلَى مُوَكِّلِهِ كَالنِّكَاحِ وَالْخُلُعِ وَالصُّلْحِ عَنْ دَمِ الْعَمْدِ فَإِنَّ حُقُوفًا تَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْمُوَكَّلِ دُونَ الْوَكِيلِ فَلَا يُطَالَبُ وَكِيلُ الزَّوْجِ بِالْمَهْرِ. (العناية: كتاب الوكالة، ج۸ ص ۱۵ ، ۱۸)
فكل عقد يضيفه الوكيل إلى نفسه أى يصح إضافته إلى نفسه ويستغنى عن إضافته إلى المؤكل (مثل البيع والإجارة ونحوهما فحقوق ذلك العقد تتعلق بالوكيل دون المؤكل لأن الوكيل فى هذا الضرب هو العاقد حقيقة، لأن العقد يقوم بكلامه، وحكما، لأنه يستغنى عن إضافة العقد إلى مؤكله...... وكل عقد يضيفه الوكيل إلى مؤكله : أى لا يستغنى عن الإضافة إلى مؤكله، حتى لو أضافه إلى نفسه لا يصح، كذا في المجتبى، وذلك كالنکاح والخلع والصلح من دم العمد ونحو ذلك فإن حقوقه تتعلق بالمؤكل) لإضافة العقد إليه (دون الوكيل)، لأنه في هذا الضرب سفير ،محض، ولذا لا يستغنى عن إضافة العقد إلى المؤكل، فكان كالرسول، وفرع على كونه سفيراً محضاً بقوله: (فلا يطالب وكيل الزوج بالمهر، ولا يلزم وكيل المرأة تسليمها للزوج، لما قلنا من أنه سفير. (اللباب) في شرح الكتاب: كتاب الوكالة، ج ۲ ص ۱۴۱)
Every contract that the agent attributes to himself, its rights pertain to the agent; and what is the opposite, its rights pertain to the principal. Translation: Every contract that the agent attributes to himself, its rights pertain to the agent; and what is the opposite, its rights pertain to the principal. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that every contract the agent attributes to himself at the time of the contract, and it is valid for him to attribute it, such as sale, purchase, and lease, etc., then all the rights of that contract, e.g., handing over the sold item, receiving the price, etc., are attached to the agent. And every contract the agent attributes to his principal at the time of the contract, such as marriage, divorce, etc., then the rights of that contract are attached to the principal. For example, the woman will demand the dower from her husband (the principal), not from the agent. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the above principle, derived that in the contract of agency for purchase, the rights are attached to the agent, i.e., delivering the sold item and paying the price and receiving the sold item are the responsibility of the agent, not the principal, because in these the agent attributes the contract to himself. And every contract in which the agent attributes to himself and it is valid to do so, the rights of that contract are, according to us, not guaranteed by destruction because compensation requires equivalence by text as known, and there is no equivalence between a commodity and a benefit. (Al-'Inayah: Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadah, vol. p. 487) And there is no equivalence between a commodity and the benefit that is the consideration, i.e., the benefit of the private part, so guarantee is not obligatory, just as in the destruction of other benefits of a usurped item, where guarantee is not obligatory according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i (al-Binayah: Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadah, vol. 6 p. 202). Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Wakalah, vol. 3 pp. 187-188. The contracts that agents conclude are of two types: a type whose rights pertain to the agent, and another to the principal. The parameter of the first: every contract that the agent attributes to himself, like sale and lease, so its rights pertain to the agent... Every contract that the agent attributes to his principal, like marriage, khul', and settlement for intentional homicide, then its rights pertain to the principal, not the agent, so the agent of the husband is not demanded for the dower. (Al-'Inayah: Kitab al-Wakalah, vol. 8 pp. 15, 18) For every contract the agent attributes to himself, i.e., it is valid for him to attribute it to himself and he is independent of attributing it to the principal (like sale, lease, and similar), so the rights of that contract pertain to the agent, not the principal, because the agent in this type is the actual contracting party, since the contract is established by his speech and legally because he is independent of attributing the contract to his principal... And every contract the agent attributes to his principal, i.e., he is not independent of attribution to his principal, such that if he attributes it to himself it is not valid, as in al-Mujtaba. That is like marriage, khul', settlement for intentional homicide, and similar. So its rights pertain to the principal due to attribution of the contract to him (not the agent), because in this type he is a mere intermediary. Hence he is not independent of attributing the contract to the principal, so he is like a messenger. And derived from his being a mere intermediary is his statement: (So the agent of the husband is not demanded for the dower, nor is the agent of the woman obliged to hand her over to the husband, because we said he is a messenger. (Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab: Kitab al-Wakalah, vol. 2 p. 141)
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of a fundamental principle in the Hanafi law of agency (wakalah). It distinguishes two categories of contracts made by an agent based on whom the contract is attributed to. The principle is: contracts that the agent validly attributes to himself (like sale and lease) impose all rights and obligations on the agent; contracts that must be attributed to the principal (like marriage, khul', settlement for intentional homicide) impose rights and obligations on the principal. The author of the Hidayah then applies this principle to specific cases. For a purchasing agent, the agent is responsible for accepting delivery and paying the price, because the contract is attributed to the agent. The text also addresses a related fiqhi issue: when a benefit (manfa'ah) is destroyed, no compensation (daman) is required according to the Hanafis, unlike the Shafi'is, because there is no equivalence between a physical commodity and a benefit. The commentary from al-'Inayah and al-Lubab reinforces the classification, explaining that in the first type the agent is the actual contracting party, while in the second he is a mere intermediary (safir). The practical consequence is that the agent of the husband cannot be sued for the dower, and the agent of the wife cannot be compelled to hand her over to the husband. This illustrates the Hanafi rule that the rights and liabilities follow the attribution of the contract.

Key Terms
وَكِيل (wakīl): An agent who is authorized by the principal (muwakkil) to perform a legal act on his behalf.
مُؤكِّل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent and for whom the agent acts.
ضَابِطَة (ḍābiṭah): A controlling rule or parameter that governs the classification of contracts in agency.
سَفِير (safīr): A mere intermediary or messenger who only conveys the contract without personal liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a marriage contract concluded by an agent for the husband, to whom does the right of dower (mahr) pertain according to the Hanafi principle?
A) The agent (wakīl)
B) The husband (muwakkil)
C) Both jointly
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The classification of agency contracts is determined by attribution: contracts attributed to the agent bind the agent; those attributed to the principal bind the principal.

The Hanafi Rule on Compensation for Destroyed Benefits in Agency
Explaining the Hanafi view on guarantee for benefits in agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that benefits are not compensable when destroyed and contrast it with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Hanafis hold that destroying a benefit does not require compensation, unlike Shafi'is who consider it property.

This lesson examines a specific branch arising from the general principle of agency contracts. The text states that when a contract attributed to the agent involves a benefit as consideration, the destruction of that benefit does not entail guarantee (daman). The Hanafi school bases this on the lack of equivalence between a commodity and a benefit. This ruling is contrasted with al-Shafi'i's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue: guarantee for destruction of benefits
Read the passage and locate where it discusses 'غير مضمونة بالإتلاف' and note the context: rights of a contract attributed to the agent are not guaranteed if the benefit is destroyed.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that no compensation (daman) is required for the destruction of a benefit (manfa'ah) in such cases.
3
Explain the Hanafi proof
The proof is that compensation requires equivalence (mumāthalah) between the lost item and the compensation, and there is no equivalence between a physical commodity ('ayn) and a benefit (manfa'ah).
This is based on a general principle that benefits are not considered property for the purpose of guarantee.
4
State the opposing school's view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that destruction of a benefit does require compensation, as he considers benefits to be property (māl).
5
Note the practical difference
In practice, if an agent or any person destroys a benefit (e.g., fails to use a hired item), Hanafis do not impose financial liability, while Shafi'is do.

ترجمہ: ہر وہ عقد جس کی نسبت وکیل اپنی طرف کرتا ہے اس کے حقوق وکیل سے متعلق ہوں گے اور جو اس کے برعکس ہو تو اس کے حقوق موکل کے ساتھ متعلق ہوں گے۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ہر ایسا عقد جس کی اضافت وقت عقد میں وکیل اپنی طرف کرے اور اس کا منسوب کرنا درست بھی ہو، مثلاً بیع وشراء اور اجارہ وغیرہ ، تو اس عقد کے تمام حقوق مثلاً بیع کا حوالہ کرنا ہشمن وصول کرنا وغیرہ وکیل سے وابستہ ہوں گے، اور ہر وہ عقد جس کی نسبت عقد کے وقت وکیل اپنے مؤکل کی طرف کرے، مثلاً نکاح، طلاق وغیرہ، تو اس عقد کے حقوق موکل سے وابستہ ہوں گے، مثلاً مہر کا مطالبہ عورت اپنے شوہر موکل سے کرے گی نہ کہ وکیل سے۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ نتلار ہے ہیں کہ وکیل با موج وکیل بالشراء میں حقوق وکیل کے ساتھ متعلق ہوں گے، یعنی مبیع سپرد کر نا ہشمن ادا کر کے مبیع وصول کرنا وکیل کی ذمہ داری ہوگی مؤکل کی نہیں ، کیونکہ ان میں وکیل عقد کی نسبت اپنی طرف کرتا ہے اور ہر وہ عقد جس میں وکیل نسبت اپنی طرف کرے اور نسبت کرنا درست بھی ہو تو اس عقد کے حقوق عِنْدَنَا غَيْرُ مَضْمُونَةٍ بِالْإِتلافِ لِأَنَّ التَّمِينَ يَقْتَضِي الْمُمَاثَلَةَ بِالنَّصِّ عَلَى مَا عُرِفَ، وَلَا مُمَاثَلَةَ بَيْنَ الْعَيْنِ وَالْمَنْفَعَةِ. (العناية: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج- ص۴۸۷) ولا مماثلة بين العين والمنفعة التى هى العوض، أعنى منفعة البضع، فلا يجب الضمان كما في إتلاف سائر منافع المغصوب، حيث لا يجب الضمان عندنا خلافا للشافعي (البناية : كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج ۶ ص ۲۰۲) الهداية كتاب الوكالة، ج ۳ ص ۱۸۷ ، ۱۸۸

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of a fundamental principle in the Hanafi law of agency (wakalah). It distinguishes two categories of contracts made by an agent based on whom the contract is attributed to. The principle is: contracts that the agent validly attributes to himself (like sale and lease) impose all rights and obligations on the agent; contracts that must be attributed to the principal (like marriage, khul', settlement for intentional homicide) impose rights and obligations on the principal. The author of the Hidayah then applies this principle to specific cases. For a purchasing agent, the agent is responsible for accepting delivery and paying the price, because the contract is attributed to the agent. The text also addresses a related fiqhi issue: when a benefit (manfa'ah) is destroyed, no compensation (daman) is required according to the Hanafis, unlike the Shafi'is, because there is no equivalence between a physical commodity and a benefit. The commentary from al-'Inayah and al-Lubab reinforces the classification, explaining that in the first type the agent is the actual contracting party, while in the second he is a mere intermediary (safir). The practical consequence is that the agent of the husband cannot be sued for the dower, and the agent of the wife cannot be compelled to hand her over to the husband. This illustrates the Hanafi rule that the rights and liabilities follow the attribution of the contract.

Key Terms
وَكِيل (wakīl): An agent who is authorized by the principal (muwakkil) to perform a legal act on his behalf.
مُؤكِّل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent and for whom the agent acts.
ضَابِطَة (ḍābiṭah): A controlling rule or parameter that governs the classification of contracts in agency.
سَفِير (safīr): A mere intermediary or messenger who only conveys the contract without personal liability.
ضَمَان (ḍamān): Legal guarantee or compensation for loss or damage.
مَنْفَعَة (manfa'ah): Benefit, usufruct, or the right to use something.
عَيْن ('ayn): Physical commodity or tangible property.

A) The agent must compensate the principal
B) The agent must compensate the third party
C) No compensation is required
D) The principal must compensate the third party

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that destroyed benefits are not compensable, unlike commodities, and this ruling contrasts with the Shafi'i view that benefits are property subject to guarantee.

Minor Ignorance is Tolerated in Agency
Stating the principle that minor ignorance does not invalidate an agency contract, with examples and proof from istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that minor ignorance (jahalah yasirah) is tolerated in agency contracts and explain the basis of istihsan (juristic preference) that overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
Minor ignorance is tolerated in agency by istihsan, unlike sale which requires precision.

In this lesson, we examine a core Hanafi ruling from Al-Hidayah: that a contract of agency (wakalah) remains valid even when there is minor vagueness or ignorance about the subject matter. This is a departure from the strict rules of sale, where such ignorance would invalidate the contract. The passage explains the principle and provides examples of general agency, citing istihsan as the overriding evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is entering into an agency contract with minor ignorance about the subject matter (e.g., description or type). The ruling is that the contract is valid (sahih).
This is the Hanafi position based on istihsan.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is istihsan, as explicitly stated: 'by istihsan'. The author notes that qiyas would reject such a contract, but the school prefers istihsan for ease.
The dalil is not a text from Quran or Sunnah but a principle of juristic preference.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The basis for istihsan is that agency is founded on seeking assistance (isti'ana) and therefore ease and convenience, unlike sale which is an exchange contract requiring certainty.
This is the ratio legis (illa) for tolerating ignorance.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Qiyas (analogy to sale) would require full specification, rendering such agency invalid. The Hanafi school chooses to override qiyas with istihsan.
This is a methodological preference; other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require more specification.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that minor ignorance is tolerated. This is from the zahir al-riwayah.
Later scholars have upheld this view as it facilitates delegation.

ترجمہ: وکالت میں معمولی جہالت برداشت کی جاتی ہے۔
۱۲۲
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ عقدِ وکالت میں تھوڑی بہت جہالت ہو تو چل سکتی ہے، مثلاً موکل بہ کی صفت اور جنس مجہول ہو، کیونکہ وکالت کی بنیاد بسبب استعانت
یسر اور سہولت پر ہے، برخلاف بیع کے۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے وکالت عامہ کے ذریعہ کسی کو وکیل بنایا، مثلا موکل نے یہ کہا کہ ابْتَعُ لِي مَا رَأَيْتَ " کہ میرے لئے وہ خرید و جو آپ مناسب سمجھیں ، تو اس طرح کی وکالت جائز ہے، یا اسی طرح وصف میں جہالت ہو، جیسے کہا کہ میرے لیے گدھایا گھوڑا یا خچر خرید و لیکن وصف بیان نہیں کیا کہ اعلی ہو یا ادنی ہو یا متوسط ہو، تو یہ وکالت درست ہے، اب وہ جس قسم کا بھی خرید لے تو یہ معاملہ درست ہوگا، کیونکہ مذکورہ صورت میں اگر چہ موکل بہ کی صفات وغیرہ بیان نہیں کیں لیکن چونکہ وکالت میں توسیع کی بناء پر معمولی جہالت برداشت کی جاتی ہے، لہذا مذکور و صورت میں یہ جہالت نظر انداز ہوگی اور یہ وکالت جائز ہوگی، اب اگر وہ کچھ بھی خریدے تو معاملہ
درست ہو گا۔
الهداية: كتاب الوكالة، باب الوكالة بالبيع و الشراء، ج ۳ ص ۱۸۹ بِخِلَافِ الْقِسْمِ الْآخَرِ وَهُوَ التَّوْكِيلُ الْعَامُّ مِثْلُ أَنْ يَقُولَ ابْتَعُ لِي مَا رَأَيْتَ فَإِنَّهُ فَوَّضَ الْأَمْرَ إِلَى رَأْيِهِ، فَأَيُّ شَيْءٍ يَشْتَرِى يَكُونُ مُمْتَيَّلًا وَيَقَعُ عَنْ الْآمِرِ وَالْأَصْلُ أَنَّ الْجَهَالَةَ الْيَسِيرَةَ مُتَحَمَّلَةٌ فِى بَابِ الْوَكَالَةِ اسْتِحْسَانًا) وَالْقِيَاسُ يَأْبَاهُ لِأَنَّ التَّوْكِيلَ بِالْبَيْعِ وَالشِّرَاءِ مُعْتَبَرٌ بِنَفْسِ الْبَيْعِ وَالشَّرَاءِ بِأَنْ يُجْعَلَ الْوَكِيلُ كَالْمُشْتَرِى لِنَفْسِهِ
Principles of Hidayah, third volume. Chapter of Agency in Sale and Purchase. (79) Minor ignorance is tolerated in agency. Translation: In agency, minor ignorance is tolerated. 122 Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that a little ignorance in the contract of agency is permissible, for example, the description and type of the object of agency are unknown, because agency, due to seeking assistance, is based on ease and convenience, unlike sale. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, states that if someone appoints an agent through a general agency, for example the principal said, 'Buy for me what you see', i.e., buy for me whatever you deem appropriate, then such agency is permissible. Or similarly, if there is ignorance in description, like he said, 'Buy for me a donkey, horse, or mule' but did not specify the description, whether high quality, low, or medium, then this agency is valid. Whatever type he buys, the transaction will be valid, because in the mentioned case, although the descriptions of the object were not stated, due to the extension in agency, minor ignorance is tolerated. Hence, this ignorance will be overlooked, and the agency will be valid. Whatever he buys, the transaction will be correct. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Wakalah, Bab al-Wakalah bi al-Bay' wa al-Shira', vol. 3 p. 189: 'Contrary to the other type, which is general agency, like when he says, "Buy for me what you see," for he delegates the matter to his opinion. So whatever he buys is considered compliant and occurs on behalf of the commander. And the principle is that minor ignorance is tolerated in the chapter of agency by istihsan. Qiyas rejects it, because agency in sale and purchase is considered analogously to the sale and purchase itself, such that the agent is like the buyer for himself.'
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental principle of Hanafi fiqh regarding agency (wakalah). The principle is that minor ignorance (jahalah yasirah) is tolerated in agency contracts. This is in contrast to sale contracts, where ignorance of the subject matter or its description invalidates the contract. The reason given is that agency is based on ease and convenience (yusr wa suhulat), whereas sale is a contract of exchange requiring precision. The author then applies this principle to two scenarios: first, a general agency (tawkil 'amm) where the principal says 'Buy for me what you see'—here the description is unknown, but the agency is valid. Second, if the principal specifies a type (e.g., donkey, horse, mule) but not the quality, the agency is also valid. The proof from Al-Hidayah confirms that istihsan (juristic preference) allows this, overriding qiyas (analogy) which would require specification. The key takeaway is that the Hanafi school prioritizes ease in agency contracts, recognizing that the purpose of agency is delegation and assistance.

Key Terms
الْجَهَالَةُ الْيَسِيرَةُ (al-jahalah al-yasirah): Minor ignorance or vagueness in the description or type of the object of agency that does not affect validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following statements correctly reflects the principle in (79)?
A) Minor ignorance invalidates an agency contract.
B) Minor ignorance is tolerated in agency contracts by istihsan.
C) Minor ignorance is only tolerated if the agent is a relative.
D) Minor ignorance is tolerated in sale contracts as well.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school tolerates minor ignorance in agency contracts by istihsan, overriding qiyas, to facilitate delegation.

The Principle in Mudarabah is Generality
Stating the principle that the default in mudarabah contracts is generality, without restrictions on cash or credit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of generality in mudarabah and apply it to resolve a dispute between rabb al-mal and mudarib.

Core Idea
Mudarabah defaults to generality – mudarib's word stands in dispute.

In Hanafi fiqh, the mudarabah contract is by default unrestricted unless explicitly conditioned. This lesson examines the principle that the mudarib is given broad authority and that in a dispute over restrictions, the mudarib's statement is preferred. The source from Al-Hidayah articulates this principle and its practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its default
Recognize that the mudarabah contract is inherently general (sahih) without needing specified conditions.
2
Understand the principle of umum
The term 'al-umum' means that no implicit restrictions are assumed; the mudarib may trade in cash or credit, etc.
This is the default position.
3
Apply to a dispute scenario
If rabb al-mal claims a restriction (e.g., cash only) and mudarib denies it, the mudarib's word is accepted because he affirms the default generality.
The burden of proof is on the one alleging a departure from the default.
4
Note the tarjih
The principle is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi; no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded.

Principles of Hidayah, third volume. 123 (80) The principle in mudarabah is generality. Translation: In mudarabah, the principle is generality. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that in the contract of mudarabah, the principle is that it is general, i.e., there should be no restriction of any kind, for example specifying the location, cash or credit, etc. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, states that if there is a dispute between rabb al-mal and mudarib regarding cash or credit, for example rabb al-mal says he imposed a restriction of cash trade, and the mudarib says he left it absolute without any restriction, then in this case the mudarib's word will be accepted, because in mudarabah the principle is generality. This is why the mudarib, upon rabb al-mal saying 'I gave the property for mudarabah', becomes the owner of disposition. The mudarib is stating the principle, and what he states... Then: 'Like a seller from the principal, and in that ignorance prevents validity, similarly in what is considered...' (Al-'Inayah: Kitab al-Wakalah, Fasl fi al-Wakalah fi al-Shira', vol. 8 p. 29) 'Except that he appoints him... this is an exception from his statement that specifying its type is necessary, meaning if he appoints him with a general agency saying "Buy for me what you see", then there is no need to mention the type and other things, because the principal delegated the matter to the agent's opinion. So whatever he buys will be compliant with the principal's order. And the principle in this chapter is that minor ignorance is tolerated in agency, like ignorance of description, by istihsan. Minor ignorance is ignorance of type, like appointment to buy a donkey, horse, mule, or cloth from Herat or Marv, which does not prevent validity of agency even if the price is not stated.' Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage presents the principle that in mudarabah contracts, the default is generality (al-umum). This means that unless explicitly restricted, the mudarib has broad authority to trade in cash or credit, at any place, etc. The practical application is that if a dispute arises between the capital provider (rabb al-mal) and the manager (mudarib) concerning whether a restriction was placed, the mudarib's statement is accepted, because he is acting on the default principle. The accompanying Arabic text, however, appears to be from the previous discussion on agency, possibly a marginal note. The key takeaway for students is that Hanafi fiqh gives primacy to the default of generality in mudarabah, protecting the mudarib's authority in the absence of explicit conditions.

Key Terms
الْعُمُومُ (al-umum): Generality, the default that no restrictions are imposed in the mudarabah contract.
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The capital provider or investor in a mudarabah contract.
مضارب (mudarib): The manager or entrepreneur who operates the mudarabah.

Baqa' al-Wakalah Ya'tamidu Qiyam al-Amr: The Continuation of Agency Depends on the Command
Explains that agency continues only as long as the principal's command exists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim regarding termination of agency, explain the qiyas underlying it, and apply it to cases of incapacity, interdiction, and partnership dissolution.

Core Idea
Agency ends automatically when the principal loses the capacity to command.

Agency (wakalah) is a contract based on the principal's authorization. But does the agent's authority survive if the principal becomes incapable? This lesson examines the Hanafi maxim that clarifies the foundation of agency: it depends on the continuous existence of the principal's command. We will explore the legal reasoning (qiyas) that extends the ruling from death to other losses of capacity, and apply it to specific cases from Al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its literal meaning
Begin by reciting the maxim in Arabic and its translation. Understand that 'baqa' al-wakalah' means the continuation of the agency, and 'qiyam al-amr' means the existence of the command. The maxim asserts that the agency remains only as long as the principal's command persists.
2
Identify the underlying legal capacity condition
Recognize that the principal's command depends on his legal capacity (ahliyyat al-ada) to command. Any event that removes this capacity eliminates the command and thus terminates the agency.
The principal must be of sound mind and not under interdiction.
3
Examine the qiyas (analogical reasoning)
The ruling for death (asl) is extended by qiyas jaliy to other cases (furu'): incapacity of a mukatib, interdiction on an authorized slave, and partnership dissolution. The illa (effective cause) is the loss of the principal's capacity to command.
Death is the clearest case (ijma'); the others share the same illa.
4
Apply the maxim to the specific cases from Al-Hidayah
Work through each case: (1) Mukatib becomes unable to pay instalments → agency void. (2) Authorized slave interdicted → agency void. (3) Partners dissolve partnership → agency void. Note that the agent's knowledge is irrelevant.
These are applications (far' ) of the general maxim.
5
Determine the ruling and its implications
Conclude that the agency becomes void (batil) immediately upon the occurrence of these events, and any transactions carried out thereafter are invalid. The agent must cease acting and return any property.
This is a hukm wad'i (declaratory ruling), not a hukm taklifi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ ثالث
باب عزل الوكيل
(۸۱) بَقَاءُ الْوَكَالَةِ يَعْتَمِدُ قِيَامَ الْأَمْرِ .
ترجمہ: وکالت کی بقاء امر کے قیام کا تقاضا کرتی ہے۔
۱۲۵
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وکالت اس وقت تک باقی رہتی ہے جب تک مؤکل کی طرف سے وکالت کا امر باقی ہو، اور موکل کے امر کا قیام موکل کی اہلیت پر مبنی ہے، لہذا جب تک مؤکل میں امر کرنے کی اہلیت ہوگی تو وکالت بھی باقی ہو گی ورنہ نہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا ر ہے ہیں کہ وکالت موکل کے مرنے سے اور جنون مطبق کے سبب مجنون ہونے سے باطل ہو جاتی ہے، اسی طرح مؤکل مکاتب تھا، مگر کتابت ادا کرنے سے عاجز آ گیا ، یا کسی عبد ماذون نے کسی کو وکیل بنایا پھر اس عبید مازون کی اجازت ختم کر دی گئی، یا دو افراد نے شرکت میں وکیل بنایا اور پھر دونوں نے شرکت ختم کر دی تو ان صورتوں میں بھی وکالت باطل ہوگی، کیونکہ وکالت کی بقاء مؤکل کی جانب سے امر کے قیام پر مبنی ہے اور مؤکل کی طرف سے امر (حکم ) کا قیام اس وقت تک ہوگا جب تک مؤکل میں اہلیت امر باقی ہو ، لیکن چونکہ موت سے، جنون مطبق سے، بعجز سے، اسی طرح حجر اور افتراق بین الشرکت سے امر کی اہلیت ختم ہو جاتی ہے، لہذا مذکورہ صورتوں میں جب مؤکل امر کا اہل نہ رہا تو موکل کی طرف سے امر قائم نہیں ہے، اور جب مؤکل کی طرف سے وکالت کا امر قائم نہیں تو وکالت کی بقاء بھی نہیں ہوگی ۔
الهداية: كتاب الوكالة، باب عزل الوكيل، ج ۳ ص ۲۰۷ وَإِذَا وَلَ الْمُكَتَبُ ثُمَّ عَجَزَ أَو العَبدُ الْمَأْذُونُ لَهُ ثُمَّ حُجِرَ عَلَيْهِ وَكَانَ التَّوكِيلُ بِالْبَيْعِ أَو الشَّرَاءِ بَطَلَتِ الْوَكَالَةُ، عَلِمَ بِذَلِكَ الْوَكِيلُ أَو لَمْ يَعْلَمُ. وَإِذَا وَكَّلَ أَحَدُ الشَّرِيكَيْنِ ثَالِيًّا بِشَيْءٍ مِمَّا لَمْ يَلِهِ بِنَفْسِهِ فَافْتَرَقَا فَكَذَلِكَ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا
Principles of Hidayah, Third Volume. Chapter: Dismissal of the Agent. (81) The continuation of the agency depends on the establishment of the command. Translation: The continuation of agency requires the existence of the command. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that agency remains as long as the command of the principal regarding the agency exists, and the existence of the principal's command is based on the principal's capacity. Therefore, as long as the principal has the capacity to command, the agency will continue, otherwise not. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, states that agency becomes invalid due to the death of the principal, or due to continuous insanity (junun mutbiq). Similarly, if the principal is a mukatib (slave under contract of manumission) and becomes unable to pay the instalments, or if an authorized slave (abd ma'dhun) appointed an agent and then his permission was revoked, or if two partners appointed an agent in a partnership matter and then dissolved the partnership – in all these cases the agency becomes invalid, because the continuation of agency is based on the existence of the command from the principal. And the command from the principal exists only as long as the principal has the capacity to command. Since death, continuous insanity, incapacity, interdiction (hajr), and dissolution of partnership eliminate the capacity to command, therefore in these cases, when the principal is no longer capable of commanding, the command from the principal does not exist, and when the command does not exist, the agency cannot continue. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Wakalah, Bab Azl al-Wakil, vol. 3, p. 207: And if a mukatib appoints an agent, then becomes incapacitated, or an authorized slave appoints an agent and then interdiction is placed upon him, and the agency was for sale or purchase, the agency becomes invalid, whether the agent knows of it or not. And if one of two partners appoints a third person as agent for something that the partner himself could not handle, and then they separate, the same applies due to what we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a legal maxim (qa'ida) from Hanafi fiqh regarding the termination of agency (wakalah). The maxim states that the continuation of agency depends on the continuation of the principal's command (amr). The author first explains the principle: agency remains valid as long as the principal has the legal capacity to issue commands. This capacity is lost through death, insanity, or any event that removes the principal's authority. The commentary then applies the maxim to several specific cases from Al-Hidayah: (1) if a mukatib (a slave who has made a contract of manumission) appoints an agent but later becomes unable to pay the instalments, the agency is void; (2) if an authorized slave appoints an agent and then his authorization is revoked by the master, the agency is void; (3) if two partners jointly appoint an agent for a partnership matter and then dissolve the partnership, the agency is void. In all these cases, the agency ends automatically, even if the agent is unaware of the principal's incapacity. The reasoning is that the principal's authority to command has ceased, and since agency is a derivative right, it cannot continue without that authority.

Key Terms
بَقَاءُ الْوَكَالَةِ (baqa' al-wakalah): The continuation of the agency contract in legal effect.
قِيَامَ الْأَمْرِ (qiyam al-amr): The existence of the principal's command or authorization.
مُكَاتَب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission (kitabah) to earn freedom by paying his owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi law, if a mukatib appoints an agent to sell his property, then becomes unable to pay his instalments, what happens to the agency?
A) The agency remains valid until the agent is informed of the incapacity.
B) The agency becomes void immediately, even if the agent is unaware.
C) The agent can complete any transactions already begun.
D) The agency is suspended until the mukatib regains ability.

Key Takeaway
The continuation of agency depends on the principal's capacity to command; any loss of that capacity automatically voids the agency.

Constructive Dismissal and Agent's Knowledge
Definition and examples of constructive dismissal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define constructive dismissal (al-azl al-hukmi), identify the scenarios where it applies, and explain why it does not require the agent's knowledge.

Core Idea
Constructive dismissal ends agency immediately, regardless of the agent's awareness.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a key principle in Hanafi agency law: when an agency terminates by operation of law rather than by the principal's explicit act, the termination is effective instantly, even if the agent remains unaware. The author clarifies that constructive dismissal occurs when the principal loses legal capacity or the underlying relationship dissolves. Understanding this rule is essential for determining the validity of transactions conducted after such events.

Guided Path
1
Define constructive dismissal
Identify the definition: termination of agency by operation of law, not by the principal's intent. The agent is dismissed involuntarily.
Contrast with explicit dismissal (al-azl al-sarih) which requires notification.
2
Identify the scenarios
List the three examples given: a mukatib becomes unable to pay, an authorized slave is interdicted, or partners dissolve their partnership. Also note death of principal.
These are cases where the principal's authority to command (amr) ceases.
3
Apply the principle
For each scenario, conclude that the agency ends immediately, and the agent's knowledge is irrelevant. The continuation of agency depends on the continuation of the command.
Analogy to death: death automatically ends agency without notification.
4
Analyze the legal reasoning
Understand the illa: loss of the principal's legal authority (amr). This is extracted by tahqiq al-manat from the death analogy. The ruling is based on qiyas.
The Qiyas panel in this lesson details the asl, far', and illa.
5
Distinguish from explicit dismissal
Note that explicit dismissal (e.g., principal says 'I dismiss you') requires the agent's knowledge to be effective, whereas constructive dismissal does not.
This difference is crucial for fatwa and court rulings.

Source Text

۱۲۶
(۸۲) اَلْعَزْلُ الْحُكْمِيُّ لَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى عِلْمِ الْوَكِيلِ . ترجمه عزل حکمی وکیل کے علم پر موقوف نہیں ہوتی۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر مؤکل کی طرف سے وکیل حکما معزول ہو جائے بایں معنی کہ مؤکل نے معزول کرنے کا کوئی قصد وارادہ نہ کیا ہو، بلکہ غیر اختیاری طور پر وکیل معزول ہو جائے تو یہ عزل وکیل کے علم پر موقوف نہیں ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ الا ر ہے ہیں کہ اگر مکاتب نے کسی کو وکیل بنایا، یا عبد مأذون نے وکیل بنایا، پھر مؤکل مکاتب بدلِ کتابت سے عاجز آ گیا اور عبد ماذون پر بندش لگ گئی تو وکیل معزول ہو جائے گا، وکیل کو عزل کا پتہ ہو یا نہ ہو، کیونکہ یہ غزل لکھی ہے، اور عزل حکمی وکیل کے علم پر موقوف نہیں ہوتا، لہذا انذکورہ صورت میں بھی وکیل کا معزول ہونا وکیل کے علم پر موقوف نہ ہوگا۔ اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے مؤکل کا انتقال ہو یعنی موکل کے مرنے سے خود بخود وکیل عزل حکمی کے سبب معزول ہو جاتا ہے، أَنَّ بَقَاءَ الْوَكَالَةِ يَعْتَمِدُ قِيَامَ الْأَمْرِ وَالافْتِرَاقِ، وَلَا فَرُقَ بَيْنَ الْعِلْمِ وَعَدَمِهِ لِأَنَّهُ عَزُلٌ حُكْمِيٌّ فَلَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى الْعِلْمِ، كَالْوَكِيلِ بِالْبَيْعِ إِذَا بَاعَهُ الْمُوَكَّلُ.
(العناية : كتاب الوكالة، باب عزل الوكيل، ج۸ ص ۱۴۴)
قوله (وإذا وكل المكاتب ثم عجز أو المأذون له فحجر عليه أو الشريكان فافترقا فهذه الوجوه تبطل الوكالة علم الوكيل أو لم يعلم لأن عجز المكاتب يبطل إذنه ،كموته، وكذا الحجر على المأذون وافتراق الشريكين يبطل إذن كل واحد منهما فيما اشتركا فيه ولأن بقاء الوكالة يعتمد بقاء الأمر، وقد بطل بالعجز والحجر والافتراق ولا فرق بين العلم ،وعدمه، لأن هذا عزل حكمى فلا يتوقف على العلم كالموت الجوهرة النيرة كتاب الوكالة، ج ۱ ص ۳۰۵)
الهداية كتاب الوكالة باب عزل الوكيل، ج ۳ ص ۲۰۷
Principles of Hidayah, Third Volume, page 126. (82) Constructive dismissal does not depend on the knowledge of the agent. Translation: Constructive dismissal is not contingent upon the agent's knowledge. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that if the agent is constructively dismissed by the principal – meaning the principal did not intend or decide to dismiss him, but the agent is dismissed involuntarily – then this dismissal does not depend on the agent's knowledge. The author of Hidayah, after stating this principle, says: if a mukatib appoints an agent, or an authorized slave appoints an agent, and then the principal (mukatib) becomes unable to pay the instalments, or interdiction is placed upon the authorized slave, the agent becomes dismissed, whether he knows of the dismissal or not, because this is constructive dismissal, and constructive dismissal does not depend on the agent's knowledge. Therefore, in these cases, the dismissal of the agent is not contingent upon his knowledge. An example of this is the death of the principal, i.e., upon the death of the principal, the agent automatically becomes dismissed by way of constructive dismissal. And the continuation of agency depends on the existence of the command, and there is no difference between knowledge and its absence, because this is constructive dismissal, so it does not depend on knowledge, like when the principal himself sells the property that was entrusted to the agent for sale. (Al-Inayah: Kitab al-Wakalah, Bab Azl al-Wakil, vol. 8, p. 144) His statement: 'And if a mukatib appoints an agent, then becomes incapacitated, or an authorized slave becomes interdicted, or two partners separate – these cases invalidate the agency whether the agent knows or not, because the incapacity of the mukatib invalidates his permission, like his death. Similarly, interdiction of the authorized slave and separation of partners invalidates the permission of each one in what they were partnered in, and because the continuation of agency depends on the continuation of the command, and that has ceased due to incapacity, interdiction, and separation. There is no difference between knowledge and its absence, because this is constructive dismissal, so it does not depend on knowledge, like death.' (Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, Kitab al-Wakalah, vol. 1, p. 305) Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Wakalah, Bab Azl al-Wakil, vol. 3, p. 207.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the termination of agency (wakalah) by introducing the concept of constructive dismissal (al-azl al-hukmi). The principle states that when an agent is dismissed by operation of law rather than by an explicit act of the principal, the dismissal is effective immediately without the agent's knowledge. The commentary explains that constructive dismissal occurs when the principal loses legal capacity (e.g., through death, insanity, or interdiction) or when the basis of the agency (e.g., partnership) is dissolved. In such cases, the agency ends automatically, and the agent's awareness is irrelevant. The text cites the same examples from Al-Hidayah as in the previous lesson: a mukatib who becomes unable to pay, an authorized slave placed under interdiction, and partners who dissolve their partnership. The author emphasizes that these are not actual dismissals by the principal but legal consequences, so they do not require notification. The analogy is drawn to the death of the principal: just as agency ends upon death without the agent being informed, so too in these cases. The quote from Al-Inayah elaborates that the incapacity of the mukatib invalidates his permission just as death does. The mention of the agent for sale (al-wakil bi al-bay') illustrates another scenario: if the principal sells the property himself, the agent's authority to sell ends constructively.

Key Terms
عَزْلٌ حُكْمِيٌّ (azl hukmi): Constructive dismissal: termination of an agency by operation of law, not by explicit act of the principal.
عِلْمِ الْوَكِيلِ (ilm al-wakil): The agent's knowledge or awareness of the dismissal.
مَأْذُون (ma'dhun): A slave who has been given permission by his master to engage in trade.

Key Takeaway
Constructive dismissal (al-azl al-hukmi) ends the agency automatically when the principal loses legal authority, and the agent's knowledge is irrelevant.

Automatic Termination of Agency Without Agent's Knowledge
Stating when agency ends automatically without agent's knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the events that cause automatic termination of agency (azl hukmi) in Hanafi fiqh and apply the ruling to novel cases without needing agent's knowledge.

Core Idea
Agency ends automatically upon certain events, regardless of the agent's knowledge.

This passage introduces the principle of 'constructive dismissal' (azl hukmi) in Hanafi law of agency. It states that agency can terminate by operation of law due to events that destroy the legal basis of the agency, and the agent's knowledge is irrelevant. The passage provides four examples: death of the principal, the principal himself performing the appointed act, the mukatab slave's contract ending, and the ma'dhun slave's permission being revoked. Understanding these events is essential to know when an agent's acts become void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
The passage states that agency terminates automatically (azl hukmi) when a fundamental change occurs, and the agent's knowledge is not required. First, note this general principle.
2
Recognize the first example: death of principal
When the principal dies, the agency ends immediately, even if the agent is unaware. The agent's acts after the death are void, as authority derived from the principal ceases.
This is because the principal's legal personality ends.
3
Recognize the second example: principal performs the act himself
If the principal personally sells the property for which the agent (wakil bil-'urj) was appointed, the agency ends. The principal's own act renders the agent's authority redundant.
The agency is specific to that sale.
4
Recognize the third and fourth examples: mukatab and ma'dhun slave
If a mukatab slave (under contract of manumission) dies or becomes incapable, or if a ma'dhun slave (permitted to trade) is interdicted, their agency terminates automatically. These are analogous to the principal's loss of capacity.
The agent's own legal capacity or the subject matter may be affected.
5
Generalize the principle
All examples illustrate that any event that destroys the legal foundation of the agency (e.g., death, loss of capacity, the principal performing the act) terminates it without knowledge. Apply this to other analogous situations.
This is based on the Hanafi maxim that agency is a contract that ends with the subject matter or capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وکیل کے لیے مؤکل کی موت کا پتہ چلنا ضروری نہیں، اسی طرح ایک شخص نے کسی کو وکیل بالعرج بنایا، پھر مؤکل نے خود اس کو فروخت کر دیا تو یہاں بھی عزل حکمی سے وکیل کی وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی اگر چہ وکیل کو اس کا پتہ نہ ہو، بالکل اسی طرح مکاتب اور عبد مازون کا مسئلہ ہے۔
It is not necessary for the agent to learn of the principal's death. Similarly, if a person made someone an agent for sale (wakil bil-'urj), then the principal himself sold it, then here too the agency ends by constructive dismissal (azl hukmi) even if the agent does not know of it. Exactly the same is the case of a mukatab and a ma'dhun slave.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the chapter of agency (wakalah). It explains the concept of 'constructive dismissal' (azl hukmi) where the agency is terminated by operation of law without the agent needing actual knowledge. The examples given are: (1) death of the principal, (2) the principal himself performing the act for which the agent was appointed (e.g., selling the property), (3) a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission) becoming incapacitated, (4) a ma'dhun slave (one permitted to trade) being interdicted. In all these cases, the agency is terminated automatically whether the agent knows or not, because the underlying basis for the agency (the principal's authority over the property or the agent's capacity) has ceased.

Key Terms
عزل حکمی (azl hukmi): Constructive dismissal of agency; termination by operation of law due to an event that makes the agency impossible or invalid, without requiring explicit revocation or knowledge.
وکیل بالعرج (wakil bil-'urj): An agent appointed specifically for a particular sale or transaction.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission (kitabah) with his master, agreeing to pay a sum to earn freedom.
عبد مازون (abd ma'dhun): A slave who has been given permission (idhn) by his master to engage in trade.

Preference by Strength, Not Multiplicity: The Hanafi Principle of Tarjīḥ
Clarifies the criterion for preferring one evidence over another in disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that preference in evidence is based on strength not multiplicity, and distinguish it from qiyas-based reasoning.

Core Idea
Preference is determined by the inherent strength of the legal cause, not the number of witnesses.

Imagine two claimants in court: one brings two witnesses for a pawn, the other brings four witnesses for a gift. Who wins? A superficial reading might favour the four witnesses, but Hanafi fiqh says otherwise. This lesson unpacks a foundational principle: tarjīḥ (preference) is based on the quality (qūwa) of the legal cause, not its quantity (kathra). We will explore this through a classic dispute and see how istiḥsān overrides qiyās.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Read the Arabic maxim: 'التَّرْجِيْحُ لَا يَقَعُ بِكَثْرَةِ الْعِلَلِ بَلْ بِقُوَّةٍ فِيْهَا' and its translation. Understand that 'causes' (ʿilal) here refer to evidence (beyyināt).
This is a uṣūlī principle applied in fiqh.
2
Analyse the qiyās argument
Identify the qiyās position: more witnesses (four) should be preferred because they provide more confirmation of the claim. In the pawn vs gift case, by qiyās, the gift is preferred because it establishes ownership directly.
3
Analyse the istiḥsān argument
Note the istiḥsān response: once the required number of witnesses (niṣāb = two) is met, additional witnesses do not increase legal strength. Preference shifts to the stronger cause: the pawn is a contract of guarantee (ḍamān), which is stronger than a gift (donation).
The strength lies in the nature of the contract, not the count.
4
Apply to the witness dispute
Consider two claimants: one with two witnesses, another with four. By istiḥsān, both are equal because each meets the niṣāb. Extra witnesses do not create tarjīḥ.
The judge must look beyond numbers to the underlying legal basis.
5
Connect to the pawn vs gift case
Recognise that the same principle applies: even if the pawn claimant has fewer witnesses (two) compared to the gift claimant (four), the pawn prevails because its cause is stronger (guarantee vs donation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التَّرْجِيْحُ لَا يَقَعُ بِكَثْرَةِ الْعِلَلِ بَلْ بِقُوَّةٍ فِيْهَا . ترجمہ: ترجیح کثرت علل کی وجہ سے واقع نہیں ہوتی، بلکہ اس میں قوت کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ علتوں کی کثرت وجہ ترجیح نہیں بن سکتی، بلکہ قوت فی الدلیل کی وجہ سے ترجیح حاصل ہوتی ہے، خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ کثرت وجہ ترجیح نہیں بن سکتی البتہ قوت وجہ ترجیح بن سکتی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ انکار ہے ہیں کہ اگر دو مدعیوں میں سے ایک نے دو گواہ پیش کئے اور دوسرے نے چار گواہ پیش کئے تو دونوں برابر ہوں گے، کیونکہ مذکورہ صورت میں ہر ایک مدعی کے دو گواہوں کی گواہی علت نام ہے، چونکہ نصاب دو گواہ ہیں، اور دونوں کے پاس نصاب مکمل ہے، البتہ ایک نے چار گواہ پیش کر کے علت میں کثرت پیدا کر دی اور کثرت کی وجہ سے علت کو ترجیح حاصل نہیں ہوتی بلکہ ترجیح قوت سے حاصل ہوتی وَهَذَا اسْتِحْسَانٌ. وَفِي الْقِيَاسِ : الْهِبَةُ أَوْلَى لِأَنَّهَا تُثْبِتُ الْمِلْكَ وَالرَّهُنُ لَا يُثْبِتُهُ) فَكَانَتْ بَيِّنَةُ الْهِبَةِ أَكْثَرَ إِثْبَاتًا فَهِيَ أَوْلَى وَجُهُ الِاسْتِحْسَانِ) أَنَّ الْمَقْبُوضَ بِحُكُم الرَّهْنِ مَضْمُونَ وَبِحُكْمِ الْهِيَةِ غَيْرُ مَضْمُونٍ، وَعَقْدُ الضَّمَانِ أَقْوَى مِنْ عَقْدِ التبرع. (العناية كتاب الدعوى، باب ما يدعيه الرجلان، ج۸ ص۲۵۷) (قَوْلُهُ وَالرَّهْنُ أَحَقُّ مِنْ الْهِبَةِ يَعْنِي لَوْ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا رَهْنَّا مَقْبُوضًا وَالْآخَرُ هِبَةً وَقَبَضَا وَبَرْهَنَا فَالرَّهُنُ أَوْلَى وَهَذَا اسْتِحْسَانٌ وَالْقِيَاسُ أَنَّ الْهِبَةَ أَوْلَى لِأَنَّهَا تُثْبِتُ الْمِلْكَ وَالرَّهُنَ لَا يُثْبِتُهُ وَوَجْهُ الِاسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَّ الْمَقْبُوضَ بِحُكْمِ الرَّهْنِ مَضْمُونٌ وَبِحُكْمِ الْهِبَةِ غَيْرُ مَضْمُونٍ وَعَقْدُ الصَّمَانِ أَقْوَى. (البحر الرائق: كتاب الدعوى، باب دعوى الرجلين، ج ص ۲۴۱ الهداية كتاب الدعوى باب ما يدعيه الرجلان، ج ۳ ص ۲۳۰
Preference does not occur due to multiplicity of causes, but due to strength in them. Translation: Preference is not established by the abundance of causes, but by the strength in them. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that the multiplicity of causes cannot be a reason for preference, rather preference is achieved by strength of evidence. In summary, multiplicity cannot be a reason for preference, but strength can be a reason for preference. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that if two claimants, one presents two witnesses and the other presents four witnesses, then both will be considered equal. Because in this case, the testimony of two witnesses from each claimant is a cause (illah). Since the required number is two witnesses, and both have completed the required number, but one has presented four witnesses, creating multiplicity in the cause. Preference is not achieved by multiplicity, but by strength. And this is istihsān. According to qiyās, the gift is preferred because it establishes ownership and the pawn does not establish it. So the evidence of gift is more effective in establishing ownership, thus it is preferred. The face of istihsān is that the item taken under pawn is guaranteed, and under gift it is not guaranteed, and the contract of guarantee is stronger than the contract of donation. (Al-Ināyah: Kitāb al-Da‘wā, Bāb mā yadda‘īhi al-rajulān, vol. 8 p. 257) (His statement: 'The pawn is more entitled than the gift' means: if one claims a pawn in possession and the other a gift in possession, and they present evidence, then the pawn is preferred. This is istihsān. And according to qiyās, the gift is preferred because it establishes ownership and the pawn does not. The face of istihsān is that the item under pawn is guaranteed, and under gift it is not guaranteed, and the contract of guarantee is stronger. (Al-Bahr al-Rā’iq: Kitāb al-Da‘wā, Bāb Da‘wā al-rajulayn, vol. p. 241) Al-Hidāyah, Kitāb al-Da‘wā, Bāb mā yadda‘īhi al-rajulān, vol. 3 p. 230.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage introduces another legal principle from Hanafi fiqh: 'Preference is not due to multiplicity of causes, but due to strength in them.' The term 'causes' (ilal) here refers to legal causes or evidence (beyyināt). The principle is applied in a dispute where two claimants present different numbers of witnesses: one with two (the minimum), the other with four. By qiyās (analogy), the one with four witnesses would be preferred because more witnesses mean stronger evidence. However, by istihsān (juristic preference), they are considered equal. The reason is that the required number (niṣāb) of witnesses is two; both have met that requirement. The additional two witnesses from one side do not add strength to the evidence; they merely multiply the cause. Preference is based on the quality (strength) of the cause, not its quantity. In this specific case, the Hanafi ruling is that both claims are treated equally. The passage then relates this back to the earlier discussion of pawn vs. gift: even though by qiyās the gift would be preferred because it establishes ownership directly, by istihsān the pawn is preferred because it is a contract of guarantee. The key takeaway is that strength in evidence or legal cause refers to its substantive nature, not numerical repetition.

Key Terms
عِلَّة ('illah): In this context, a cause or legal evidence, often referring to testimony (shahādah) as a means of proof.
تَرْجِيح (tarjīḥ): Preference given to one evidence or claim over another when they conflict.
نِصَاب (niṣāb): The minimum required number of witnesses for a proof; in testimony, two male witnesses or one male and two females.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The claimant with four witnesses wins because they have more evidence.
B) Both claims are considered equal because both meet the required minimum of two witnesses.
C) The judge will order a new hearing with additional evidence.
D) The claimant with two witnesses wins because they had fewer witnesses.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, tarjīḥ is determined by the strength of the underlying legal cause, not the multiplicity of evidence.

The Principle of Unconditional Confession
Stating a fundamental rule of iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a confession (iqrar) must be unconditional and apply it to identify invalid conditional confessions.

Core Idea
A confession suspended on a condition is void — iqrar demands certainty.

In Hanafi law, a confession (iqrar) is a definitive acknowledgment of an existing right, such as a debt. This passage introduces a key rule: iqrar cannot be conditional. If someone says 'I owe you 1000 dirhams, if Allah wills,' the confession is invalid because it introduces uncertainty. Let us examine why and how this principle works.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Identify the core legal statement: 'al-iqrar la yahtamil al-ta'liq bi al-shart' – a confession does not admit of being suspended on a condition.
2
Understand the nature of iqrar
Recall that iqrar is an acknowledgment of an existing right, not a promise or a contingent statement. It must be immediate and definitive.
This is why conditions introduce doubt and invalidate the confession.
3
Apply to the example
Consider the example: 'so-and-so owes me one thousand dirhams, if Allah wills.' The phrase 'in sha Allah' makes the confession conditional on Allah's will, creating uncertainty.
The confessor either nullifies the confession or suspends it, both unacceptable.
4
Determine the ruling
Conclude that the confession is invalid (batil) and no obligation arises. The mufta bihi position is that such a confession cannot be enforced.
This is a clear-cut rule with no exceptions in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاستثناء
( ١٠١) اَلْإِقْرَارُ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ التَّعْلِيقَ بِالشَّرُطِ . ترجمہ: اقرار شرط پر معلق کرنے کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر مقر اقرار کرتا ہے لیکن اقرار کو کسی شرط پر معلق کرتا ہے تو اقرار درست نہ ہوگا اور یہ استثناء معتبر ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے کسی حق کا اقرار کیا اور ساتھ ہی ان شاء اللہ کہا، مثلا "الفلان عَلَيَّ أَلْفُ دِرْهَم إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ " کہا تو اقرار درست نہ ہوگا اور مقر پر کوئی چیز لازم نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ جب مقر نے ان شاء اللہ کے ساتھ استثناء کیا تو اس نے یا تو اپنے اقرار کو باطل کر دیا یا اللہ تعالی کی مشیت پر معلق کر دیا،
Chapter of Exception (Istithna) (101) Confession does not tolerate suspension by a condition. Translation: Confession does not admit of being suspended on a condition. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that if a person makes a confession but suspends it on a condition, the confession is not valid and this exception is considered. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if someone confesses a right and says 'in sha Allah', e.g., 'so-and-so owes me one thousand dirhams, if Allah wills', then the confession is not valid and nothing is incumbent upon the confessor, because when the confessor made an exception with 'in sha Allah', he either nullified his confession or suspended it on the will of Allah.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement establishing that a valid iqrar (confession/acknowledgment) cannot be made conditional or suspended upon a future event. The example given is adding 'in sha Allah' to a confession of debt. Since 'in sha Allah' implies a condition of Allah's will, the confession becomes uncertain and thus unenforceable. The commentary explains that this is because the exception (istithna) either voids the confession or makes it contingent on divine will, which is incompatible with the nature of iqrar as a definitive declaration of an existing obligation. The principle is that an iqrar must be clear, immediate, and unconditional.

Key Terms
الإقرار لا يحتمل التعليق بالشرط (al-iqrar la yahtamil al-ta'liq bi al-shart): A legal rule that a confession (iqrar) is invalid if it is made conditional on a future event, because iqrar is an assertion of an existing right, not a promise or contingent statement.
استثناء (istithna): An exception made in a statement, here specifically referring to the phrase 'in sha Allah' used to suspend a confession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says, 'I owe you one thousand dirhams, in sha Allah,' what is the ruling?
A) The confession is valid and the debt is due
B) The confession is invalid and nothing is due
C) The confession is valid only if the condition occurs
D) The confession is valid but the debt is reduced

Key Takeaway
An iqrar (confession) must be unconditional; any suspension on a future event renders it invalid.

intermediate
7 min
Acknowledgment Cannot Be Conditional
Ruling with proof from Quran and Hanafi usul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that an acknowledgment (iqrar) cannot be conditional, identify the proof from the Quran, and apply the principle of bara'at al-dhimma to resolve doubt.

Core Idea
An acknowledgment is a report of the past; a condition concerns the future, so conditional acknowledgment is void.

In Islamic law, an acknowledgment (iqrar) is a powerful declaration that creates a liability. However, the Hanafi school insists that such an acknowledgment must be unconditional. Why? Because iqrar is essentially a report (khabar) of an existing obligation, and reports are not suspended on future events. This lesson unpacks that reasoning, examines a supporting Quranic verse, and explores how ambiguity triggers the principle that liabilities are presumed free until proven.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon and the legal classification. The act is an acknowledgment (iqrar) made conditional on a future event. The ruling is that such an acknowledgment is invalid (batil).
The text gives the example of saying 'I owe one thousand dirhams if Allah wills.'
2
Locate the proof and rationale
Why is conditional iqrar invalid? The text explains that iqrar is a report (khabar), and a report cannot be suspended. Acknowledgment informs about a past or present obligation, while a condition pertains to the future—a logical contradiction.
The proof is based on the nature of iqrar, not a direct text, but the text uses the Quranic verse to illustrate ambiguity in a related case.
3
Analyze the linguistic ambiguity
The text discusses a case: if someone says 'a garment among ten garments,' only one garment is binding according to Abu Yusuf. This is because the particle 'fee' (in/among) is ambiguous—it can mean 'in' or 'between,' causing doubt.
The Quranic verse 'Enter among My servants' (Al-Fajr 89:29) is cited to show that 'fee' can mean 'between.'
4
Apply the principle of bara'at al-dhimma
Since doubt exists about the intended meaning, the principle that liabilities are originally free (bara'at al-dhimma) applies. One cannot impose an obligation beyond what is certain. Therefore, only the minimum (one garment) is binding.
This principle is invoked to avoid burdening a person without clear evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر مقر اقرار کرتا ہے لیکن اقرار کو کسی شرط پر معلق کرتا ہے تو اقرار درست نہ ہوگا اور یہ استثناء معتبر ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے کسی حق کا اقرار کیا اور ساتھ ہی ان شاء اللہ کہا، مثلا "الفلان عَلَيَّ أَلْفُ دِرْهَم إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ " کہا تو اقرار درست نہ ہوگا اور مقر پر کوئی چیز لازم نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ جب مقر نے ان شاء اللہ کے ساتھ استثناء کیا تو اس نے یا تو اپنے اقرار کو باطل کر دیا یا اللہ تعالی کی مشیت پر معلق کر دیا، اور اقرار فى البين والوسط أيضاً، قال الله تعالى: فَادْخُلِي فِي عِبَادِي) (الفجر : ٢٩) أى بین عبادی فوقع الشك) لأن كلمة فى لما استعملت في معنى "بين كما استعملت للظرف لم يلزمه إلا ثوب واحد لوقوع الشك فيما زاد عليه، فلا يجوز والمال لا يجب بالشك والاحتمال والأصل براءة الذمم) لأنها خلقت برية عرية عن الحقوق، فلا يجوز شغلها إلا بحجة قوية (البناية: كتاب الإقرار، ج ۹ ص ۴۴۴) وَإِنْ قَالَ ثَوبٌ فِى عَشَرَةِ أَثْوَابِ لَمْ يَلْزَمُهُ إِلَّا ثَوبٌ وَاحِدٌ عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ) ..... وَلَا بِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّ حَرْفَ فِى يُسْتَعْمَلُ فِى الْبَيْنِ وَالْوَسَطِ أَيْضًا، قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى فَادْخُلِي فِي عِبَادِى) (الفجر: (۲۹) أَى بَيْنَ عِبَادِى فَوَقَعَ الشَّكُ فِي أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِحَرْفِ فِي هَاهُنَا مَعْنَى الظَّرْفِ أَوْ مَعْنَى الْبَيْنِ، وَبِالشَّكِّ لَا يَثْبُتُ مَا زَادَ عَلَى الْوَاحِدِ وَالأصْلُ بَرَاءَةُ الدِّمَمِ لِأَنَّهَا خُلِقَتْ بَرِيئَةً عَرِيَّةٌ عَنْ الْحُقُوقِ فَلَا يَجُوزُ شَغْلُهَا إِلَّا بِحُجَّةٍ قَوِيَّةٍ. فتح القدير : كتاب الإقرار، ج۸ ص ۳۴۲)

تعلیق کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا، کیونکہ اقرار خبر کی قبیل سے ہے اور خبر معلق نہیں ہوتی ، اس لیے کہ اقرار گزرے ہوئے زمانے میں واقع کی خبر دینا ہے، اور ماضی اور مستقبل کے درمیان منافات ہے، لہذا مذکورہ صورت میں اقرار باطل ہوگا۔ نیز اللہ کی مشیعیت کا بھی علم نہیں ، لہذا اس اقرار کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔
Chapter of Exception (Istithna). (101) Acknowledgment does not bear suspension upon a condition. Translation: Acknowledgment does not have the capacity to be suspended on a condition. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that if the acknowledger makes an acknowledgment but suspends it on a condition, the acknowledgment is not valid and this exception will be considered. The author of Al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that if someone acknowledges a right and also says 'in sha Allah', for example says 'So-and-so owes me one thousand dirhams if Allah wills', then the acknowledgment is not valid and nothing is binding upon the acknowledger. Because when the acknowledger made an exception with 'in sha Allah', he either nullified his acknowledgment or suspended it upon the will of Allah, and acknowledgment... also in the middle and between, Allah said: 'Enter among My servants' (Al-Fajr:29) meaning 'between My servants', so doubt occurs. Because the word 'fee' is used in the meaning of 'between' as it is used for 'in', so only one garment is binding due to doubt about what is additional, so it is not permissible, and wealth is not obligated by doubt and probability, and the principle is the innocence of liabilities because they are created free and bare of rights, so it is not permissible to occupy them except with strong evidence. (Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Iqrar, vol.9 p.444) And if he says 'a garment among ten garments', only one garment is binding upon him according to Abu Yusuf... and according to Abu Yusuf, the particle 'fee' is also used in the meaning of 'between' and 'middle', Allah said: 'Enter among My servants' meaning 'between My servants', so doubt occurs about whether the intended meaning of 'fee' here is the meaning of 'in' or 'between', and with doubt, what is more than one is not established, and the principle is the innocence of liabilities because they are created free and bare of rights, so it is not permissible to occupy them except with strong evidence. (Fath al-Qadir: Kitab al-Iqrar, vol.8 p.342) (Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Iqrar, Chapter of Istithna, vol.3 p.242) It does not bear suspension, because acknowledgment is of the category of information (khabar), and information is not suspended, because acknowledgment is informing about an event in the past, and there is a contradiction between past and future, so in the mentioned form the acknowledgment is null. Also, Allah's will is not known, so this acknowledgment will not be considered.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage presents the first principle from the chapter on Istithna (exception) in the book of Acknowledgment (Iqrar) from Al-Hidayah. The ruling is that an acknowledgment (iqrar) cannot be made conditional upon a future event, because iqrar is a report (khabar) of something that has already occurred. Suspension (ta'liq) applies to future events, so there is a contradiction. The text gives the example of someone saying, 'I owe one thousand dirhams if Allah wills.' This is invalid as an acknowledgment. The commentator explains that the person either intended to nullify the acknowledgment or to suspend it on Allah's will—both are impermissible. The passage also discusses a related issue: if someone says, 'a garment among ten garments,' only one garment is binding according to Abu Yusuf, due to the ambiguity of the word 'fee' (in/among). The Quranic verse 'Enter among My servants' is cited to show that 'fee' can mean 'between,' causing doubt about what is intended. The principle of bara'at al-dhimma (presumption of innocence of liability) is invoked: a person's liability is originally free, and cannot be burdened without strong evidence. The passage emphasizes that doubt prevents obligation.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession of a right or liability.
تعلیق (ta'liq): Suspension of a legal effect upon the occurrence of a future condition.
استثناء (istithna): An exception made by excluding something from a general statement.
براءة الذمم (bara'at al-dhimam): The legal principle that a person's liability (dhimma) is originally free of obligations; claims must be proven.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The acknowledgment is valid and binding.
B) The acknowledgment is invalid and nothing is owed.
C) The acknowledgment is valid only if the condition occurs.
D) The acknowledgment is valid but the amount is reduced.

Key Takeaway
Acknowledgment is a report of an existing obligation; any condition on a future event invalidates it because doubt cannot establish liability.

Istithna Operates on the Uttered Word, Not Meaning
Principle: istithna acts on wording, not meaning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that istithna operates only on the literal wording (malfuz) and apply it to determine the validity of exceptions in acknowledgment cases.

Core Idea
Istithna only excludes what the words explicitly include — implied meanings are not affected.

This passage from Al-Hidayah introduces a fundamental rule of istithna (exception) in the Hanafi school: an exception only affects what is literally expressed, not what is included by meaning. This principle has direct consequences in contracts and acknowledgments, where a poorly worded exception may be entirely ineffective. We will explore the rule, its application to a house-and-building example, and why it matters in practice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of istithna
Istithna is a legal tool that excludes part of a general statement. The key question is: what does it operate on — the wording or the intended meaning?
2
Analyze the principle 'tasarruf fi al-malfuz'
According to the Hanafi school, istithna is a disposal in the uttered word (tasarruf fi al-malfuz). This means it only affects things that are explicitly mentioned in the mustathna minhu (the thing from which exception is made).
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the nature of speech and the need for certainty in legal transactions.
3
Apply to the house and building example
If someone acknowledges a house (dar) and says 'except the building' (bina), the building is conceptually part of the house but is not explicitly mentioned in the acknowledgment. Since istithna operates on wording, the exception is invalid, and the beneficiary receives both the house and the building.
The building is included by meaning (ma'nan), not by wording (lafzan).
4
Connect to the rule on conditional acknowledgments
The passage reiterates that acknowledgment (iqrar) is a report of the past and cannot be suspended on a condition (ta'liq). This supports the idea that istithna must be immediate and based on clear wording, not future conditions or implied meanings.
This is a secondary point; the main focus remains on the operation of istithna.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۰۲) الاسْتِثْنَاءُ تَصَرُّفٌ فِي الْمَلْفُوظِ. •
ترجمہ: استثناء لفظ میں تصرف کا نام ہے۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ استثناء مستثنی منہ کے لفظ سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ معنی سے، یعنی مستثنی منہ جن چیزوں کو از راہ لفظ شامل ہو ان سے استثناء کرنا درست ہے اور جن چیزوں کو از راہ معنی شامل ہو ان کا استثنا صحیح نہ ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر مقر نے مقرلہ کے لئے دار (گھر) کا اقرار کیا اور بناء کا استثناء کیا تو مقرلہ کے لیے دار اور بناء دار دونوں ہوں گے، کیونکہ بناء دار میں معنوی طور پر تبعا داخل ہوتی ہے لفظ نہیں، اور استثناء اس چیز کا درست ہوتا ہے جسے لفظ مستثنی منہ شامل ہو، کیونکہ استثناء لفظ میں عمل کرتا ہے معنی میں نہیں، لہذا یہ وَإِنْ كَانَ الثَّانِي فَكَذَلِكَ، إِمَّا لِأَنَّ الْإِقْرَارَ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ التَّعْلِيقَ بِالشَّرْطِ لِأَنَّ الْإِقْرَارَ إِخْبَارٌ عَمَّا سَبَقَ وَالتَّعْلِيقُ إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ وَبَيْنَهُمَا مُنَافَاةٌ .
(العناية: كتاب الإقرار، باب الاستثناء وما في معناه، ج۸ ص ۳۵۷) (فَإِنْ كَانَ الْأَوَّلُ وَهُوَ الْإِبْطَالُ فَقَدْ بَطَلَ وَإِنْ كَانَ الثَّانِي وَهُوَ التَّعْلِيقُ فَكَذَلِكَ، إِمَّا لِأَنَّ الْإِقْرَارَ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ التَّعْلِيقَ بِالشَّرْطِ لِأَنَّ الْإِقْرَارَ إِخْبَارٌ عَمَّا سَبَقَ وَالتَّعْلِيقُ إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ وَبَيْنَهُمَا مُنَافَاةٌ.
(فتح القدير : كتاب الإقرار، باب الاستثناء وما في معناه، ج۸ ص ۳۵۷) الهداية كتاب الإقرار باب الاستثناء، ج ۳ ص ۲۴۲
(102) Istithna (exception) is an operation in the uttered word (malfuz). Translation: Exception is the name for a disposal in the utterance. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that istithna is made from the literal wording of the thing from which exception is made (mustathna minhu), not from its meaning. That is, it is valid to exclude things that are included in the mustathna minhu by way of wording, and it is not valid to exclude things that are included by way of meaning. The author of Al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that if the acknowledger acknowledges a house (dar) for the beneficiary and excludes the building (bina), then the beneficiary will get both the house and the building, because the building is included in the house conceptually as a dependent, not by wording. And istithna is valid only for something that the wording of the mustathna minhu includes, because istithna operates on the wording, not on the meaning. Hence this: 'and if it is the second, then likewise, either because acknowledgment does not bear suspension upon a condition, because acknowledgment is a report of what has passed, and suspension is only in relation to the future, and there is a contradiction between them.' (Al-Inayah: Kitab al-Iqrar, Chapter of Istithna and what is in its meaning, vol.8 p.357) 'If it is the first, which is nullification, then it is null; and if it is the second, which is suspension, then likewise, either because acknowledgment does not bear suspension upon a condition, because acknowledgment is a report of what has passed, and suspension is only in relation to the future, and there is a contradiction between them.' (Fath al-Qadir: Kitab al-Iqrar, Chapter of Istithna and what is in its meaning, vol.8 p.357) (Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Iqrar, Chapter of Istithna, vol.3 p.242)
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage presents the second principle from the chapter on Istithna: that exception operates on the uttered word, not on the implied meaning. The commentator explains that if someone acknowledges a house and then makes an exception of the building (i.e., says 'except the building'), that exception is not effective because the building is conceptually part of the house but is not explicitly mentioned in the wording. The building is included by meaning as a necessary component, but istithna only affects what the wording covers. Therefore, the beneficiary receives both the house and the building. The passage then repeats the earlier principle about acknowledgment not being conditional, tying it back to the nature of istithna. The references to Al-Inayah and Fath al-Qadir confirm this ruling.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna): The legal act of excluding something from a general statement, operating on the wording.
تصرف في الملفوظ (tasarruf fi al-malfuz): An operation that affects the literal wording, not the underlying meaning.
مستثنى منه (mustathna minhu): The general term from which the exception is made; the base statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone acknowledges a house (dar) and says 'except the building' (bina), what is the ruling in the Hanafi school?
A) The building is excluded from the acknowledgment.
B) The acknowledgment is invalid due to contradiction.
C) Both the house and the building are included in the acknowledgment.
D) The acknowledgment is valid but the building is excluded by intention.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an exception only removes what the words explicitly include — anything included only by meaning remains part of the original statement.
