Priority of Debts with Known Causes over Acknowledged Debts in Terminal Illness
Establishing the priority of debts with known causes over mere acknowledgements in marad al-mawt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on priority of debts in marad al-mawt and apply the principle that an acknowledgement nullifying another's right is invalid.

Core Idea
Debts with known causes take priority over mere acknowledgements in terminal illness to protect prior creditors.

In this passage, Al-Marghinani sets forth a critical rule concerning the distribution of a terminally ill debtor's assets. When a debtor acknowledges new debts while already owing others from health or known causes, the prior debts take precedence. The author provides the proof: any acknowledgement that would nullify a prior creditor's right is invalid. This lesson unpacks that principle and its analogy to other transactions like rahn (pledge) and ijara (lease).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the passage to determine the exact rule: which debts take precedence? The text states that debts of health and debts with known causes (e.g., compensation for destroyed property, mahr) are given priority over debts merely acknowledged during terminal illness.
The ruling applies only when the debtor is in marad al-mawt (terminal illness).
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author cites the principle: 'An acknowledgement is not considered if it involves nullifying another's right' (الإقرار غير معتبر إذا تضمن إبطال حق الغير). This is supported by analogy to rahn and ijara, where a debtor cannot dispose of property if it harms creditors.
The proof is from general fiqh principles, not a direct nass.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the dalil proves the ruling)
The acknowledged debt in marad al-mawt would compete with prior creditors, effectively nullifying their right to satisfaction. Since an acknowledgement that nullifies another's right is invalid, the prior debts must be paid first.
The link is the illa of nullifying another's right (ibṭāl ḥaqq al-ghayr).
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
The passage is from a Hanafi text; it implies a difference with other schools that might treat all acknowledgements equally. The Hanafi view protects prior creditors by prioritizing debts with known causes.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the practical consequence is different distribution of the estate.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi. Al-Marghinani, supported by 'Inayah and Tabyeen al-Haqaiq, confirms this as the relied-upon position.
The authority weight is zahir_riwayah; no intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned.

صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ انتلار ہے ہیں کہ اگر مریض مرض الموت میں اپنے اوپر دیون کا اقرار کرتا ہے، جبکہ اس پر حالت صحت کے دین اور کچھ ایسے قرض ہیں جو حالت مرض میں ہوئے ، مگر لوگوں کو وہ قرض معلوم ہیں، تو حالت صحت کے دین اور معروفہ الاسباب دین کو پہلے ادا کیا جائے گا، جیسے کسی کی کوئی چیز ہلاک کی ، یا بیوی کے مہر کی ادائیگی باقی ہے، یا کسی سے کوئی چیز خریدی جو معلوم ہے، اس کے شمن کی ادائیگی باقی ہے، تو اس طرح دیون جن کے اسباب معلوم ہیں تو اُن کی ادائیگی پہلے ہوگی، کیونکہ مریض مرض الموت میں دین کا اقرار کر کے ان قرض خواہوں کا حق باطل کرنا چاہتا ہے جن کے قرضے اس پر حالت صحت میں ہوئے تھے یا اس کے حالت مرض میں لوگوں کے معلومات کے مطابق ہوئے تھے اور ایسا اقرار جس میں غیر کے حق کا ابطال آتا ہو وہ دلیل نہیں بن سکتا، لہذا اس کا یہ اقرار بھی بطور دلیل معتبر نہ ہو گا ، اس لیے حالت صحت کے دین اور معروفتہ الاسباب دین جو حالت مرض میں ہوئے اور لوگوں کو معلوم ہیں، ان ) کو مقر بہ دین پر مقدم کیا جائے گا۔ قَالَ (وَإِذَا أَقَرَّ الرَّجُلُ فِي مَرَضِ مَوْتِهِ إِلَخُ إِذَا مَرِضَ الْمَدْيُونُ وَلَزِمَهُ دُيُونٌ حَالَ مَرَضِهِ بِأَسْبَابِ مَعْلُومَةٍ مِثْلُ بَدَلِ مَالِ مِلْكِهِ أَوْ اسْتَهْلَكَهُ أَوْ مَهْرُ مِثْلِ امْرَأَةٍ تَزَوَّجَهَا وَعَلِمَ مُعَايَنَةً أَوْ أَقَرَّ فِي مَرَضِهِ بِدُيُونٍ غَيْرِ مَعْلُومَةِ الْأَسْبَابِ فَدُيُونُ الصَّحَّةِ وَالَّتِي عُرِفَتْ أَسْبَابُهَا مُقَدَّمَةٌ عَلَى الدُّيُونِ الْمُقَرِّ بِهَا .... (وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْإِقْرَارَ غَيْرُ مُعْتَبَرٍ إِذَا تَضَمَّنَ إِبْطَالَ حَقَّ الْغَيْرِ وَإِقْرَارُ الْمَرِيضِ تَضَمَّنَهُ، لَّانَّ حَقَّ غُرَمَاءِ الصَّحَّةِ تَعَلَّقَ بِهَذَا الْمَالِ اسْتِيفَاءً وَلِهَذَا مُنِعَ مِنْ التَّبَرُّعِ وَالْمُحَابَاةِ أَصْلًا إِذَا أَحَاطَتْ الدُّيُونُ بِمَالِهِ وَبِالزِّيَادَةِ عَلَى الثُّلُثِ. (العناية: كتاب الإقرار، باب إقرار المريض، ج۸ ص ۳۸۰) وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْإِقْرَارَ غَيْرُ مُعْتَبَرٍ إِذَا كَانَ فِيهِ إِبْطَالُ حَقِّ الْغَيْرِ، أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّهُ إِذَا رَهَنَ عَيْنًا أَوْ آجَرَهُ لَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَتَصَرَّفَ فِيهِ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنْ إِبْطَالِ حَقِّ الْغَيْرِ وَهُنَا أَيْضًا فِي إِقْرَارِهِ بِذَلِكَ، لأَنَّ حَقَّ أَصْحَابِ الدُّيُونِ تَعَلَّقَ بِمَالِهِ اسْتِيفَاء، وَلِهَذَا مُنِعَ مِنْ التَّبَرُّعِ وَالْمُحَابَاةِ مُطْلَقًا فِي حَقِّهِمْ غَيْرَ مُقَدَّرِ بِالثُّلُثِ . (تبيين الحقائق: كتاب الإقرار باب إقرار المريض، ج ۵ ص ۲۴ )
The author of Al-Hidayah mentions this principle and explains that if a sick person in terminal illness acknowledges debts upon himself, while he has debts from health and some debts that occurred during illness but are known to people, then the debts of health and those with known causes will be paid first. For example, if he destroyed someone's property, or owes his wife's mahr, or purchased something known, then payment of the price remains. So debts with known causes are paid first because the sick person by acknowledging debts in terminal illness intends to nullify the right of those creditors whose debts were incurred during health or during illness with known causes. Such an acknowledgement that involves nullifying another's right cannot be considered a proof, therefore his acknowledgement will not be valid as a proof. Hence, debts of health and debts with known causes that occurred during illness and are known to people will be given priority over the acknowledged debt. He said: When a man acknowledges in his terminal illness... when a debtor becomes sick and debts become due upon him during his illness due to known causes, such as compensation for property that he owned or destroyed, or the dowry of a woman he married and she was known, or he acknowledges in his illness debts with unknown causes, then the debts of health and those whose causes are known are given precedence over the debts acknowledged. And our proof is that acknowledgement is not considered if it involves nullifying another's right. And the acknowledgement of a sick person involves that, because the right of the creditors from health is attached to this wealth for satisfaction, and therefore he is prevented from donating and showing favoritism absolutely when debts encompass his wealth and beyond one-third. (Al-'Inayah: Kitab al-Iqrar, Bab Iqrar al-Marid, vol.8 p.380) And our proof is that acknowledgement is not considered if there is nullification of another's right. Do you not see that if he pledges a specific property or leases it, he does not have the right to dispose of it because of nullification of another's right. And here also in his acknowledgement of that, because the right of the creditors is attached to his wealth for satisfaction, and therefore he is prevented from donating and showing favoritism absolutely in their right without restriction to one-third. (Tabyeen al-Haqaiq: Kitab al-Iqrar, Bab Iqrar al-Marid, vol.5 p.24)
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Hanafi fiqh regarding the priority of debts in the case of a person who is terminally ill (marad al-mawt). The author begins by explaining the ruling: when a person in terminal illness acknowledges debts (i.e., confesses owing money) while already having debts from his period of health or debts during illness that are known to people (e.g., through a known cause), the debts from health and those with known causes take precedence over the debts he acknowledges in his terminal illness. This is because the acknowledgement that nullifies the prior rights of creditors is invalid. The text then quotes from Al-Hidayah: the ruling is that debts of health and those with known causes are given priority over acknowledged debts. The proof (dalil) is that an acknowledgement which involves nullifying another person's right is not valid (ghayr mu'tabar). The right of the creditors from the period of health has already attached to the debtor's wealth for satisfaction; therefore, the debtor is prevented from making donations or showing favoritism, especially when debts encompass his entire estate. The same principle applies to other transactions like pledging or leasing: if a debtor's action nullifies a creditor's right, it is not valid. So here, the acknowledgement in terminal illness would nullify the prior creditors' right to be satisfied, so it is not considered. The authority weight: This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah as it appears in Al-Hidayah and the references to Al-'Inayah and Tabyeen al-Haqaiq confirm it. The Hanafi position is clear: debts with known causes (from health or known events in illness) are muqaddam (given priority) over debts acknowledged in illness. There is no intra-Hanafi dispute mentioned here. The mufta bihi is as stated.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession of a debt or right. In this context, the dying person's admission of debts.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Terminal illness where the person is predominantly likely to die. Special rules apply to prevent fraud.
الدين المعروف السبب (al-dayn al-ma'ruf al-sabab): Debts with known causes, e.g., from a purchase or destruction of property, as opposed to mere acknowledgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Debts with known causes (from health or known events in illness) must be prioritized over mere acknowledgments in terminal illness to prevent nullifying prior creditors' rights.

Contracts Interpreted by Meanings: The Principle and Its Application to Sulh
Explaining the legal maxim that contracts are interpreted by their substance, not wording, and applying it to sulh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim that contracts are interpreted by their meanings, and apply it to classify a sulh contract as a sale or hire based on its substance.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, the substance of a contract determines its rulings, not its name.

This lesson unpacks a key principle from Al-Hidayah: contracts are judged by their underlying purpose, not their labels. You'll see how this maxim works in practice by examining the contract of sulh (compromise), which can be treated as a sale or a hire depending on what is being exchanged. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying contract rulings in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Identify the Arabic maxim: 'الاعتبار في العقود للمعاني' (Consideration in contracts is for meanings). Understand that the legal effect depends on the substance (ma'na) of the contract, not the words used.
This is a foundational rule in Hanafi contract law.
2
Grasp the rationale
The purpose of contracts is to achieve the intended meanings (e.g., exchange of property, transfer of usufruct). Therefore, the law looks at the real nature of the transaction.
Parties cannot circumvent mandatory rules by using different names.
3
Apply to sulh with acknowledgment (iqrar)
When a sulh is made after the defendant acknowledges the claim and the settlement involves property for property, the meaning of the contract is sale (bay'). Hence, all sale rulings apply: return due to defect, pre-emption, options of condition and sight, etc.
This is the first application mentioned in the text.
4
Distinguish the usufruct case
When sulh involves property (the claim) in exchange for usufruct (e.g., using a car or house), the meaning is hire (ijarah). The rulings of ijarah apply, such as specifying the duration.
This shows the principle is consistently applied.
5
Derive the ruling consequences
Based on the classification, all subsidiary rulings of the underlying contract (sale or hire) become effective. The name 'sulh' does not change the legal nature.
This principle prevents manipulation of contract types.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ ثالث
كتاب الصلح
(١٠٢) اَلْاِعْتِبَارُ فِي الْعُقُودِ لِلْمَعَانِي.
ترجمہ: عقود میں اعتبار معانی کا ہوتا ہے۔
۱۵۲
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جتنے بھی عقود ہیں مثلاً عقد بیع ، عقد اجارہ وغیرہ ان میں اعتبار معانی کا ہوتا ہے نہ کہ الفاظ کا ، یعنی حکم معانی پر مرتب ہوگا، اس لیے کہ مقصود معانی ہوتے ہیں۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر صلح اقرار سے ہو یعنی مدعی علیہ نے اقرار کیا اور پھر مدعی کے ساتھ مال کے دعوی کے عوض مال سے صلح کر لی تو اس صلح میں ان تمام احکامات کا اعتبار ہوگا جن کا بیج میں اعتبار کیا جاتا ہے، مثلاً عیب کی وجہ سے واپس کرنا ، زمین میں شفعہ کا ثابت ہونا ، خیار شرط اور خیار رؤیت کا ثابت ہونا وغیرہ، کیونکہ جب صلح مال سے مال پر واقع ہوا تو اس میں بیچ کا معنی ( مبادلة المال بالمال ) پایا گیا۔ اسی طرح اگر مال کے عوض منافع پر صلح ہوئی، مثلا مدعی پچاس ہزار کا مطالبہ کر رہا ہے اور مدعی علیہ اسے اپنی گاڑی سوار ہونے کے لیے دے دی، یا اپنا مکان رہنے کے لیے دے دیا ، تو یہ اجارہ ہوگا اور اس میں اجارہ کے احکام ملحوظ ہوں گے یعنی مدت کا بیان کرنا وغیرہ، کیونکہ صلح جب مال کے دعوی پر منافع سے ہوا تو اس میں اجارہ کا معنی ( تملیک المال بالمنافع ) پایا گیا ہے، اور اعتبار عقد میں معانی کا ہوتا ہے اور عقد صلح بھی ایک عقد ہے، لہذا اس میں بھی اعتبار
Principles of Hidayah, Part Three
Chapter of Sulh
(102) Consideration in contracts is for meanings.
Translation: In contracts, consideration is given to meanings.
Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that whatever contracts there are, for example, contract of sale, contract of hire, etc., in them consideration is given to meanings, not to words, meaning the ruling will be attached to the meanings, because the intended matter is meanings.
The author of Al-Hidayah mentions this principle and is explaining that if a compromise (sulh) occurs upon acknowledgement, i.e., the defendant acknowledges, and then makes a compromise with the plaintiff in exchange for property over a claim of property, then in this compromise all the rulings that are considered in a sale will be considered, for example, returning due to defect, the establishment of pre-emption (shuf'ah) in land, the establishment of option of condition (khiyar al-shart) and option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah), etc., because when the compromise is based on property for property, the meaning of sale (exchange of property for property) is found. Similarly, if a compromise is made on usufruct in exchange for property, for example, the plaintiff is claiming fifty thousand and the defendant gives him his car to ride, or gives his house to live in, then it will be a hire (ijarah) and the rulings of hire will be observed, such as specifying the duration, etc., because when the compromise is on a claim of property in exchange for usufruct, the meaning of hire (ownership of property for usufruct) is found. And consideration in contracts is for meanings, and the contract of compromise is also a contract, so consideration in it is also for meanings.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental legal maxim in Hanafi fiqh: contracts are interpreted according to their meanings, not their literal wording. The author first states the maxim in Arabic: 'الاعتبار في العقود للمعاني' (Consideration in contracts is for meanings). He then provides an Urdu explanation: in all types of contracts, such as sale and hire, the legal effect is based on the underlying substance (ma'na) rather than the words used, because the purpose of contracts is to achieve the meanings. The author of Al-Hidayah applies this maxim to the contract of sulh (compromise/settlement). If a sulh is made with acknowledgment (iqrar) by the defendant, and the settlement is for property in exchange for a property claim, then this sulh is treated as a sale (bay'), and all the rules of sale apply: return due to defect, pre-emption, options of condition and sight, etc. This is because the meaning of sulh in that case is exchange of property for property, which is the same as sale. If the sulh is for usufruct (manafi') in exchange for a property claim, then it is treated as a lease (ijarah), and the rules of ijarah apply, including specification of duration. The principle is consistently applied: the real nature of the transaction determines its rulings, not what the parties call it. This is an important principle in Hanafi contract law, ensuring that parties cannot circumvent mandatory rules by using different names. The authority weight: This principle is well-established in the Hanafi school and is from the Zahir al-Riwayah as it appears in Al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): Compromise or settlement of a dispute by mutual agreement, often involving payment or property.
معنى (ma'na): Meaning, substance, or underlying legal purpose of a contract.
اعتبار (i'tibar): Consideration, regard, or legal weight given to something.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if two parties make a settlement (sulh) where one party gives his car for two months of use in exchange for the other dropping a claim of money, what type of contract is this?
A) Sale (bay')
B) Hire (ijarah)
C) Gift (hibah)
D) Loan (qard)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the contract of sulh is classified by its underlying meaning—sale if property-for-property, hire if property-for-usufruct—and the name used does not alter the applicable rulings.

Interpreting a Sane Person's Transaction as Valid
States the principle of validating a sane person's transaction and provides a counterexample

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of interpreting a sane person's transaction as valid and identify the two exceptions where this principle does not apply.

Core Idea
A sane person's transaction is upheld as valid whenever possible, but not when it infringes on Allah's rights or another person's rights.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, we encounter a foundational Hanafi maxim: a sane, mature person's legal act should be interpreted in a manner that upholds its validity. This reflects the school's overall tendency to preserve transactions (ihkam al-tasarrufat). However, the author immediately qualifies it with concrete cases—sulh in hadd claims and paternity disputes—showing that the principle has limits.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Recite the Arabic maxim and its English translation. This is the core legal principle.
Memorize the exact wording: 'تصرف العاقل يتحرى تصحيحه ما أمكن'.
2
Define key terms
Understand the three key terms: tasarruf (legal transaction), 'aqil (sane, mature person), and taharrin (seeking the correct interpretation).
'Aqil implies sanity and maturity (bulugh).
3
Identify the exceptions
Two examples are given: (1) sulh in hadd claims (for zina, theft, or drinking), where the settlement is void because it involves Allah's right; (2) sulh in a paternity dispute, where a woman settles lineage for money, because lineage is the child's right.
The principle does not apply when the transaction involves compensation for another's right without permission.
4
Explain the rationale
The principle cannot validate transactions that violate explicit prohibitions (e.g., taking compensation for Allah's right or a third party's right). These rights are non-negotiable.
In Hanafi fiqh, hadd for slander (qadhf) is also considered Allah's right, not the victim's personal right.
5
Recognize the limit
The principle is a hermeneutic tool: it guides judges and jurists to prefer validity, but it is overridden by clear textual prohibitions.
This maxim is often cited in contracts to avoid nullification due to minor ambiguities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١٠٦) تَصَرُّفَ الْعَاقِلِ يُتَحَرَّى تَصْحِيحُهُ مَا أَمْكَنَ.
ترجمہ: جہاں تک ممکن ہو عاقل کے تصرف کو صحیح قرار دینے کے لئے کوشش کی جائے گی۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ عاقل بالغ آدمی کے تصرف کو حتی الامکان قَالَ (وَلَا يَجُوزُ عَنْ دَعْوَى حَدَّ الْأَصْلُ فِى هَذَا أَنَّ الْاعْتِبَاضَ عَنْ حَقِّ الْغَيْرِ لَا يَجُوزُ، فَإِذَا أَخَذَ رَجُلٌ زَانِيَا أَوْ سَارِفًا أَوْ شَارِبَ خَمْرٍ وَأَرَادَ أَنْ يَرْفَعَهُ إِلَى الْحَاكِمِ فَصَالَحَهُ الْمَأْخُوذُ عَلَى مَالِ لِيَتُرُكَ ذَلِكَ فَالصُّلْحُ بَاطِلٌ ... وَإِذَا ادَّعَتْ امْرَأَةٌ عَلَى رَجُلٍ صَبِيَّا هُوَ بِيَدِهَا أَنَّهُ ابْنُهُ مِنْهَا وَجَحَدَ الرَّجُلُ وَلَمْ تَدَّعِ الْمَرْأَةُ النِّكَاحَ وَقَالَتْ إِنَّهُ طَلَّقَهَا وَبَانَتْ مِنْهُ وَصَدَّقَهَا فِي الطَّلَاقِ فَصَالَخَ مِنْ النَّسَبِ عَلَى مِائَةِ دِرْهَم فَالصُّلْحُ بَاطِلٌ لِأَنَّ النَّسَبَ حَقُّ الصَّبِيِّ فَلَا يَجُوزُ الاعْتِيَاضُ عَنْهُ.
(العناية: كتاب الصلح، فصل الصلح عن دعوى الأموال، ج۸ ص ۴۱۸) قوله ولا يجوز فى دعوى حد لأنه حق الله لا حقه ولا يجوز الاعتياض عن حق غيره ولهذا لا يجوز الاعتياض إذا ادعت المرأة نسب ولدها، لأنه حق الولد لا حقها وسواء كان الحد في سرقة أو قذف أو زنا أما الرنا والسرقة فلأن الحد فيه حق الله تعالى بلا خلاف . وأما حد القذف فإنه أيضا حق الله تعالى عندنا. (الجوهرة النيرة كتاب الصلح، ج ۱ ص ۳۲۰)
الهداية كتاب الصلح باب الصلح في الدين، ج ۳ ص ۲۵۶
(106) A sane person's transaction should be sought to be validated as much as possible. Translation: Effort should be made to validate the transaction of a sane person as much as possible. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that the transaction of a sane, mature person should be [validated] as much as possible. He said: (And it is not permissible in a claim of hadd; the principle in this is that taking compensation for another's right is not permissible. So if a man seizes a fornicator, a thief, or a wine drinker and intends to bring him to the judge, and the seized person makes sulh with him for property to leave that, then the sulh is void... And if a woman claims against a man that a child in her custody is his son from her, and the man denies, and the woman does not claim marriage and says that he divorced her and she is separated from him, and he confirmed her in divorce, and she makes sulh from the lineage for one hundred dirhams, then the sulh is void because lineage is the right of the child, so taking compensation for it is not permissible. (al-'Inayah, Kitab al-Sulh, Section on sulh in claims of properties, j8 p418) He said: And it is not permissible in a claim of hadd because it is the right of Allah, not his right, and taking compensation for another's right is not permissible. For this reason, taking compensation is not permissible when a woman claims the lineage of her child, because it is the right of the child, not her right. Whether the hadd is for theft, slander, or zina: as for zina and theft, the hadd is undeniably the right of Allah. As for the hadd of slander (qadhf), it is also the right of Allah according to us. (al-Jawharah al-Nirah, Kitab al-Sulh, j1 p320) al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Sulh, Section on sulh in debt, j3 p256.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage introduces the principle that the transactions of a sane, mature person should, as far as possible, be interpreted and upheld as valid. This is a fundamental rule in Hanafi fiqh for preserving people's dealings and avoiding nullification. However, the author immediately provides a counterexample: the case of sulh in hadd claims. Even though the parties are sane adults, their sulh is invalid because it involves compensation for Allah's right, which is not permissible. The same applies to a woman settling a paternity claim for money, since lineage is the child's right. The passage thus clarifies that the principle of validation has limits: it cannot override explicit prohibitions or rights of others. The commentary from al-'Inayah and al-Jawharah reiterates the earlier principle that taking compensation for another's right is not allowed, and specifically notes that according to the Hanafi school, hadd for slander (qadhf) is also a right of Allah, unlike the Shafi'i view.

Key Terms
تصرف (tasarruf): A legal transaction or disposal of property or rights.
عاقل ('aqil): A sane person of sound mind, usually also implying maturity (bulugh).
تحري (taharrin): To seek and strive for the correct interpretation or application.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the limit of the principle that a sane person's transaction should be validated as much as possible?
A) It applies only to sales and not to leases
B) It does not apply when the transaction involves a right of Allah or another person without permission
C) It applies only to transactions involving property
D) It applies only if both parties are sane

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'tasarruf al-'aqil yutaharra tashihuhu' reflects a pro-validity presumption, but it is bounded by the inviolability of Allah's rights and third-party rights.

Hands Differ in Trustworthiness: The Principle of Inalienable Trust in Wadi'ah
Stating the principle that hands vary in trustworthiness and its legal effect in deposits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim 'al-aydi takhtalifu fi al-amanah' and apply it to determine when a depositary becomes liable for loss of a deposited item.

Core Idea
A depositary cannot transfer the deposit to another without consent—the owner's trust is specific to the depositary's hand.

In the chapter of wadi'ah (deposits), Hanafi jurists invoke a succinct yet powerful maxim: 'Hands differ in trustworthiness.' This principle clarifies that the legal classification of possession varies with the person; not every hand is equally trustworthy. When a depositary entrusts the deposit to a third party without the owner's permission, he exceeds the bounds of trust and becomes liable for any subsequent loss. This lesson unpacks the maxim, its foundation, and its practical application in determining liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim
Read the maxim 'al-aydi takhtalifu fi al-amanah' and grasp its literal meaning: hands differ in trustworthiness. Recognize that this is a legal principle, not a mere observation.
The maxim is specific to Hanafi fiqh and appears in Kitab al-Wadi'ah of Al-Hidayah.
2
Understand the Legal Implication
The maxim implies that each person's possession (yad) carries its own level of trust. The owner's consent is given to the depositary's specific hand, not to any hand in general. Therefore, transferring the deposit to another is a breach of trust (ta'addi).
This distinguishes yad amanah (trustworthy possession) from yad dhaman (guarantor possession).
3
Apply the Maxim to Wadi'ah
If a depositary gives the deposit to a third party (not part of his household) without the owner's permission, he has violated the trust. The maxim dictates that the owner only consented to the depositary's hand, so the depositary becomes liable (dhamin) for the item.
The same ruling applies analogously to mudarabah and wakalah when delegation occurs without authorization.
4
Determine the Ruling
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that the depositary is liable regardless of the third party's apparent trustworthiness. This is because the breach is in the unauthorized transfer itself, not in the character of the recipient.
Al-Hidayah records this as the zahir al-riwayah position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْأَيْدِي تَخْتَلِفُ فِي الْأَمَانَةِ
Hands differ in trustworthiness.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational principle in the chapter of wadi'ah (deposits). It means that not all persons who take possession (yad) of property are equally reliable. Some are trustworthy (amin), others are treacherous. The author of Al-Hidayah invokes this principle to explain the ruling that if a depositary (mudi') entrusts the deposited item to someone other than his own household without the owner's permission, and the item is destroyed, the depositary becomes liable (dhamin). The reasoning: the owner consented to the depositary's possession, not to that of a third party. Since the depositary exceeded the bounds of trust (ta'addi) by placing the item in an untrustworthy hand, he must guarantee its value. The same rule applies analogously to a mudarib or agent who cannot delegate without authorization. The principle also distinguishes between yad amanah (trustworthy possession) and yad dhaman (guarantor possession); the former does not incur liability for loss, but the latter does when the act of entrustment is improper. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi maxim that amanah is not transferable without consent.

Key Terms
الأيدي تختلف في الأمانة (al-aydī takhtalifu fī al-amānah): A legal maxim meaning that the legal classification of possession (yad) varies in terms of trustworthiness; some hands are trustworthy (yad amanah) and others are treacherous (yad khiyanah).
مودع (mūdiʿ): The depositary; the person with whom an item is deposited for safekeeping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling based on this principle, if a person deposits his goods with a friend, and the friend gives them to his neighbor (not a household member) for safekeeping without the owner's permission, and the goods are destroyed, what is the ruling?
A) The friend is not liable because the neighbor was trustworthy
B) The friend is liable because he exceeded his trust by giving the deposit to an unauthorized person
C) The neighbor is liable for accepting the deposit
D) The owner bears the loss because he chose the friend

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'al-aydi takhtalifu fi al-amanah' establishes that a depositary becomes liable for loss whenever he transfers the deposit to an unauthorized hand, regardless of the recipient's trustworthiness.

The Principle of Differing Hands in Trust
Explaining ruling on depositary liability for delegation to non-family

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a depositary becomes liable for entrusting a deposit to a non-family member, and explain the underlying principle of differing hands.

Core Idea
A depositary becomes liable if he entrusts the deposit to an unapproved hand, because trusts differ in trustworthiness.

The Hanafi school of fiqh has a nuanced approach to deposit (wadi'ah). One key principle is that 'hands differ in trust' — not every person who holds property is equally trustworthy. In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario from al-Hidayah: what happens when a depositary passes the deposit to someone outside his household without the owner's permission. The ruling hinges on transgression (ta'addi) and the owner's implicit consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Start with the statement 'al-aydi takhtalifu fi al-amanah' — hands/possessions differ in trust. Understand that this principle governs the liability of trustees.
The principle is foundational for determining when a trustee becomes liable.
2
State the Ruling
If a depositary entrusts the deposit to a non-family member (ghayr 'iyalihi) without the owner's permission, and the deposit is destroyed, the depositary becomes liable (damin).
Family members (iyal) are assumed trustworthy by the owner's implicit consent.
3
Identify the Reason: Ta'addi
The depositary has committed ta'addi (transgression) by deviating from the owner's consent. The owner agreed to his possession only, not to another's.
Ta'addi is the key concept that transforms a trustee into a guarantor.
4
Note the Analogy with Mudarabah and Wakalah
The same logic applies: a mudarib cannot appoint another mudarib without permission, nor a wakil appoint another wakil. The 'thing' does not include its like.
This analogy strengthens the ruling via qiyas.

بعض امانت کی حفاظت کرتے ہیں اور بعض امانت میں خیانت کرتے ہیں۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر موزع نے اپنے اہل دعیال کے علاوہ کسی اور سے ودیعت کی حفاظت کرائی ، یا کسی اجنبی کو آگے بطور ودیعت دے دیا اور ودیعت ہلاک ہوگی تو مودع ضامن ہوگا، کیونکہ امانت میں قبضے مختلف ہوتے ہیں، بعض تو امانت داری کا ثبوت دیتے ہیں اور بعض خائن ہوتے ہیں اور چونکہ مالک اس کے پاس تو امانت رکھنے پر راضی تھا، لیکن دوسرے کے پاس امانت رکھنے پر راضی نہیں تھا، اس لیے مودَع نے امانت میں تعدی کی ، لہذا وہ ضامن ہوگا۔ شے اپنے مثل کو متضمن نہیں ہوتی ، جیسے ایک مضارب بغیر اجازت کے دوسرے کو مضارب بنائے ، یا ایک وکیل دوسرے کو اپنا وکیل بنائے ، تو یہ درست نہیں ہے، اسی طرح اگر ایک شخص کے پاس امانت رکھوائی
جائے تو وہ مالک کی اجازت کے بغیر دوسرے کے پاس امانت نہیں رکھوا سکتا، اس لیے کہ

Principles of Hidayah, Third Volume. Book of Deposit. (112) The hands differ in trust. Translation: Possessions differ in trust. 162 Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that people's possessions in trust are different: some protect the trust and some betray the trust. The author of Hidayah mentioned this principle to explain that if the depositary entrusted the deposit to someone other than his own family members for preservation, or gave it forward as a deposit to a stranger, and the deposit perished, then the depositary is liable, because possessions in trust differ: some prove trustworthiness and some are treacherous. And since the owner consented to keep the trust with him but did not consent to keep it with another, therefore the depositary committed transgression in the trust, so he is liable. An item does not include its like, just as a mudarib cannot make another mudarib without permission, or a wakil cannot make another wakil, so it is not valid. Similarly, if someone deposits a trust with a person, he cannot entrust it to another without the owner's permission, because he trusts him, not the other. (Then an Arabic quote from al-Binaayah: 'The owner of capital (said: No, it is not as you mentioned, but) I gave you two thousand as mudarabah, so the statement is the statement of the mudarib because the dispute in reality is about the amount received, restricted because if the dispute is about the description, then the statement is of the owner of capital as will come. And in its like, i.e., in the like of the dispute about the amount received, the statement is of the receiver, whether he was a guarantor, i.e., the receiver like a usurper, or a trustee, i.e., or he was a trustee like the depositary. (al-Binaayah: Book of Mudarabah, Chapter on the mudarib giving mudarabah, Section on dispute between owner and mudarib, vol. 10 p. 102) al-Hidayah: Book of Deposit, vol. 3 p. 276)
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational principle in the Hanafi law of deposit (wadi'ah): 'al-aydi takhtalifu fi al-amanah' (possessions/hands differ in trustworthiness). The author uses this principle to explain the ruling when a depositary (mustawda') entrusts the deposit to someone outside his household (ghayr 'iyalihi). The ruling: if the depositary gives the deposit to a non-family member for safekeeping or forwards it to another person as a deposit, and the deposit is destroyed, the depositary becomes liable (damin). The reason is that the owner consented to the depositary's possession but not to another's, and since possessions vary in trustworthiness, the depositary has committed transgression (ta'addi) by exposing the deposit to an unapproved hand. The passage draws an analogy (qiyas) with mudarabah (silent partnership) and wakalah (agency): just as a mudarib cannot appoint another mudarib without permission, nor a wakil appoint another wakil, similarly a depositary cannot delegate the deposit without the owner's consent. The additional Arabic quote from al-Binaayah on mudarabah confirms the procedural rule that in a dispute over the amount received, the statement of the receiver is accepted regardless of whether he is a guarantor or trustee, but this is a tangential reference.

Key Terms
وديعة (wadi'ah): A contract of deposit where one party leaves his property with another for safekeeping without compensation.
أمانة (amanah): Trust; the legal status of property held by a person who is not liable for loss unless he transgresses.
ضامن (damin): Liable; guarantor; one who must compensate for loss or damage.
تعدي (ta'addi): Transgression; exceeding the bounds of proper conduct in handling the trust.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The depositary is not liable because the deposit was not misused.
B) The depositary is liable because he transgressed by giving it to an unapproved hand.
C) The depositary is liable only if the stranger was a known thief.
D) The depositary is not liable because the loss was accidental.

Key Takeaway
A depositary becomes liable for loss if he entrusts the deposit to a non-family member without the owner's permission, because possession of a trust implies personal responsibility.

Condition That Is Useless or Impossible Is Void (Al-Shartu Yalghu)
Second principle: useless/impossible conditions are void

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that a useless or impossible condition in a deposit contract is void and does not affect the depositary's liability.

Core Idea
A condition that is useless or impossible to fulfill is void; the contract remains valid without it.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a depositary must follow the depositor's valid conditions. But what if the condition is impossible to fulfill or provides no benefit? The Hanafi school rules that such conditions are void (yalghu), and the depositary is not bound by them. This prevents hardship and upholds the purpose of the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its nature
Determine whether the condition has a practical legal effect (mufid) and whether it is possible to act upon (mumkin al-'amal).
2
Apply the test of benefit
If the condition has no benefit (ghayr mufid), it is void regardless of possibility.
3
Apply the test of possibility
Even if beneficial, if acting upon it is impossible (e.g., because the depositary must use a specific person), the condition is void.
4
Determine liability consequence
Since the condition is void, the depositary remains a trustee (amin) and is not liable for loss when acting out of necessity.

Source Text

(۱۱۳) اَلشَّرُطُ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنُ مُفِيدًا أَوْ كَانَ وَلَمْ يُمْكِنِ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ يَلْغُوُ. ترجمہ: شرط جب مفید نہ ہو یا مفید ہو ، لیکن اس پر عمل کرنا ممکن نہ ہو تو وہ شرط الغو ہوگی ۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر مودع ایسی شرط لگائے جس کا کوئی فائدہ نہ ہو، یا فائدہ تو ہولیکن اس شرط پر عمل کرنا ممکن نہ ہو تو وہ شرط الغو ہوگی، موقع پر اس کی رعایت رکھنا ضروری نہیں ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے اس بات کو بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر مودع نے مودع کو کہا کہ یہ ودیعت اپنی زوجہ کو نہ دینا، پھر مودع نے زوجہ کو دے دی جبکہ مودع اپنی بیوی کو دیئے بغیر اس کی حفاظت نہیں کر سکتا اس کے علاوہ کوئی چارہ کار نہیں ہے اور وہ چیز بلاک بھی ہو گئی تو موذع ضامن نہ ہو گا، اسی طرح چو پایہ تھا اور یہ شرط لگائی کہ اپنے غلام کو نہ دینا، حالانکہ غلام کو دیئے بغیر اُس کا کوئی چارہ کار نہیں ہے، اور وہی جانوروں کا خیال کرتا ہے، اب مودع نے ایسی شرط لگائی جس پر عمل کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے، کیونکہ آدمی بذات خود (فَإِنْ حَفِظَهَا بِغَيْرِهِمْ بِأَنْ تَرَكَ بَيْتًا فِيهِ الْوَدِيعَةُ وَخَرَجَ وَفِيهِ غَيْرُ عِيَالِهِ أَوْ أَوْدَعَهَا غَيْرَهُمْ بِأَنْ نَقَلَهَا مِنْ بَيْتِهِ وَأَوْدَعَهَا عِنْدَ غَيْرِهِمْ (ضَمِنَ، لِأَنَّ الْمَالِكَ رَضِيَ بِيَدِهِ لَا بِيَدِ غَيْرِهِ وَ الْحَالُ أَنَّ الْأَيْدِيَ تَخْتَلِفُ فِي الْأَمَانَةِ). (العناية: كتاب الوديعة، ج ۸ ص ۴۸۷) قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ (وَإِنْ حَفِظَهَا بِغَيْرِهِمْ ضَمِنَ أَى بِغَيْرِ مَنْ فِي عِبَالِهِ، لِأَنَّ صَاحِبَهَا لَمْ يَرْضَ بِيَدِ غَيْرِهِ وَالْأَيْدِى تَخْتَلِفُ فِي الْأَمَانَةِ، وَلَانَّ الشَّيْءَ لَا يَتَضَمَّنُ مِثْلَهُ كَالْمُضَارِبِ لَا يُضَارِبُ . تبيين الحقائق: كتاب الوديعة، ج ۵ ص ۷۷)
الهداية كتاب الوديعة، ج ۳ ص ۲۷۹
(113) A condition, if it is not beneficial or if it is beneficial but its implementation is not possible, is void. Translation: A condition, when it is not beneficial, or it is beneficial but acting upon it is not possible, then that condition is void. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that if the depositor makes a condition that has no benefit, or it has benefit but acting upon that condition is not possible, then that condition is void, and it is not necessary to observe it. The author of Hidayah mentioned this principle to explain that if the depositor said to the depositary, 'Do not give this deposit to your wife,' then the depositary gave it to his wife, while the depositary could not protect it without giving it to his wife and had no alternative, and the item was lost, then the depositary is not liable. Similarly, if it was an animal, and the condition was made that 'Do not give it to your slave,' even though the depositary had no alternative without giving it to the slave, and the slave was the one who tends the animals, then the depositor made a condition whose implementation is not possible. Because a person himself (Then an Arabic quote from al-Hidayah: 'If he kept it with other than them, i.e., by leaving a house containing the deposit and going out while in it were other than his family, or he entrusted it to other than them, i.e., by moving it from his house and entrusting it with other than them, he is liable, because the owner consented to his possession, not the possession of another, and the fact is that hands differ in trust.') (al-Inayah: Book of Deposit, vol. 8 p. 487) He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And if he kept it with other than them, he is liable, i.e., with other than those in his household, because its owner did not consent to the possession of another, and hands differ in trust, and because a thing does not include its like, as the mudarib does not make another mudarib.' (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Book of Deposit, vol. 5 p. 77)
al-Hidayah: Book of Deposit, vol. 3 p. 279
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents a second principle from the chapter on wadi'ah: a condition that is either useless (ghayr mufid) or impossible to fulfill (la yumkin al-'amalu bihi) is void (yalghu). The author illustrates this with a scenario: the depositor stipulates that the depositary must not give the deposit to his wife (or slave). However, if the depositary cannot protect the deposit without involving his wife or slave, then the condition is impossible to fulfill. In such a case, the depositary does not become liable if he gives the deposit to his wife or slave out of necessity. The condition is void, and the ruling returns to the default rule: the depositary is a trustee (amin) and is not liable for loss. The passage then supports this with a quote from al-Hidayah and other commentaries stating that if the depositary gives the deposit to someone outside his household without necessity, he is liable, but here the impossibility of fulfilling the condition negates liability. The quote also reiterates the earlier principle that hands differ in trust. This shows that in Hanafi fiqh, conditions that are contrary to the nature of the contract or impossible are disregarded to prevent hardship.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition or stipulation attached to a contract by one of the parties.
الغو (yalghu): It is void; null and of no legal effect.
مفيد (mufid): Beneficial; having a practical legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle in lesson 2, what is the ruling if a depositor stipulates that the depositary should not give the deposit to anyone, but the depositary cannot protect it without doing so?
A) The condition is binding, and the depositary becomes liable if he gives it to anyone.
B) The condition is void, and the depositary is not liable if he gives it to someone out of necessity.
C) The deposit becomes invalid due to the impossible condition.
D) The depositor must take back the deposit if the condition cannot be fulfilled.

Key Takeaway
A condition in a deposit that is useless or impossible is automatically void, and the depositary is not liable for acting contrary to it out of necessity.

Void Conditions in Deposit: When Impossibility Nullifies Liability
Explaining the principle of void conditions in wadiah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a condition is void if useless or impossible, and apply it to determine the depositary's liability in deposit scenarios.

Core Idea
A condition impossible to fulfill is void; the depositary is not liable for violating it.

In Hanafi fiqh, a condition in a contract is binding only when it provides benefit and can be practically observed. This lesson focuses on a key ruling in the law of deposit (wadi'ah): when a depositor imposes a condition that the depositary cannot realistically fulfill—such as not entrusting the deposit to his wife when she is the only available person—the condition becomes legally void (laghw). Consequently, the depositary incurs no liability if the deposit is lost after violating that condition. Understanding the criteria of benefit and possibility is essential for correctly assigning liability in trust-based contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the General Principle
Recall the rule: a condition that is not beneficial (ghayr mufid) or is beneficial but impossible to fulfill (la yumkin al-'amal bihi) is void (yalghu). The depositary is not obliged to observe it.
This principle appears in al-Hidayah and is supported by al-Jami' al-Saghir.
2
Identify the Condition and Its Feasibility
In the given scenario, identify the exact condition (e.g., 'Do not give the deposit to your wife'). Ask: Does the depositary have an alternative person to safeguard the deposit? Is he able to comply without abandoning the deposit's safety?
If he has no other option (la budda lahu), the condition is impossible to fulfill.
3
Apply the Principle to the Condition
If the condition is impossible to fulfill, it is void (laghw). If the condition is beneficial and possible, observing it is wajib.
The text emphasizes that possibility is the key determinant.
4
Determine Liability
If the condition is void, the depositary is not liable (daman) for loss following violation. If the condition is valid and the depositary had an alternative but violated it, he is liable.
Liability (daman) arises only when the depositary had a feasible choice and chose to contravene.

اصول ہدایہ ثالث جائے تو وہ مالک کی اجازت کے بغیر دوسرے کے پاس امانت نہیں رکھوا سکتا، اس لیے کہ اُسے اس پر اعتماد ہے دوسرے پر نہیں۔ (۱۱۳) اَلشَّرُطُ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنُ مُفِيدًا أَوْ كَانَ وَلَمْ يُمْكِنِ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ يَلْغُوُ. ترجمہ: شرط جب مفید نہ ہو یا مفید ہو ، لیکن اس پر عمل کرنا ممکن نہ ہو تو وہ شرط الغو ہوگی ۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر مودع ایسی شرط لگائے جس کا کوئی فائدہ نہ ہو، یا فائدہ تو ہولیکن اس شرط پر عمل کرنا ممکن نہ ہو تو وہ شرط الغو ہوگی، موقع پر اس کی رعایت رکھنا ضروری نہیں ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے اس بات کو بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر مودع نے مودع کو کہا کہ یہ ودیعت اپنی زوجہ کو نہ دینا، پھر مودع نے زوجہ کو دے دی جبکہ مودع اپنی بیوی کو دیئے بغیر اس کی حفاظت نہیں کر سکتا اس کے علاوہ کوئی چارہ کار نہیں ہے اور وہ چیز بلاک [؟] بھی ہو گئی تو موذع ضامن نہ ہو گا، اسی طرح چو پایہ تھا اور یہ شرط لگائی کہ اپنے غلام کو نہ دینا، حالانکہ غلام کو دیئے بغیر اُس کا کوئی چارہ کار نہیں ہے، اور وہی جانوروں کا خیال کرتا ہے، اب مودع نے ایسی شرط لگائی جس پر عمل کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے، کیونکہ آدمی بذات خود (فَإِنْ حَفِظَهَا بِغَيْرِهِمْ بِأَنْ تَرَكَ بَيْتًا فِيهِ الْوَدِيعَةُ وَخَرَجَ وَفِيهِ غَيْرُ عِيَالِهِ أَوْ أَوْدَعَهَا غَيْرَهُمْ بِأَنْ نَقَلَهَا مِنْ بَيْتِهِ وَأَوْدَعَهَا عِنْدَ غَيْرِهِمْ (ضَمِنَ، لِأَنَّ الْمَالِكَ رَضِيَ بِيَدِهِ لَا بِيَدِ غَيْرِهِ وَ الْحَالُ أَنَّ الْأَيْدِيَ تَخْتَلِفُ فِي الْأَمَانَةِ). (العناية: كتاب الوديعة، ج ۸ ص ۴۸۷) قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ (وَإِنْ حَفِظَهَا بِغَيْرِهِمْ ضَمِنَ أَى بِغَيْرِ مَنْ فِي عِبَالِهِ، لِأَنَّ صَاحِبَهَا لَمْ يَرْضَ بِيَدِ غَيْرِهِ وَالْأَيْدِى تَخْتَلِفُ فِي الْأَمَانَةِ، وَلَانَّ الشَّيْءَ لَا يَتَضَمَّنُ مِثْلَهُ كَالْمُضَارِبِ لَا يُضَارِبُ . تبيين الحقائق: كتاب الوديعة، ج ۵ ص ۷۷) الهداية كتاب الوديعة، ج ۳ ص ۲۷۹

 اصول بدایہ ثالث چوبیس گھنٹہ ودیعت کی حفاظت نہیں کرتا بلکہ اپنی بیوی کے پاس رکھتا ہے، یا جانوروں کی دیکھے بال عموماً نوکر چاکر کرتے ہیں۔ اب بیوی اور غلام لا پرواہ اور غافل بھی نہیں، تو یہ ایسی شرط ہے جس پر عمل ممکن نہیں اور ہر ایسی شرط جس پر عمل کرنا ممکن نہ ہو وہ لغو ہوتی ہے، لہذا مورع کی یہ شرط بھی لغو ہوگی۔ (وَإِذَا قَالَ صَاحِبُ الْوَدِيعَةِ لِلْمُودَعِ لَا تُسَلَّمُهَا إِلَى زَوْجَتِكَ فَسَلَّمَهَا إِلَيْهَا لَا يَضْمَنُ مَعْنَاهُ: إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مِنْ التَّسْلِيمِ إِلَيْهَا بُةٌ، عُلِمَ ذَلِكَ مِنْ رِوَايَةِ الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ حَيْثُ قَالَ إِذَا نَهَاهُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَهَا إِلَى أَحَدٍ مِنْ عِيَالِهِ فَدَفَعَهَا إِلَى مَنْ لَا بُدَّ لَهُ مِنْهُ لَا يَضْمَنُ، كَمَا إِذَا كَانَتْ الْوَدِيعَةُ دَابَّةٌ فَنَهَاهُ عَنْ الدَّفْعِ إِلَى غُلَامِهِ، أَوْ كَانَتْ شَيْئًا يُحْفَظُ عَلَى أَيْدِى النِّسَاءِ فَنَهَاهُ عَنْ الدَّفْعِ إِلَى امْرَأَتِهِ وَهَذَا مَعْنَى قَوْلِهِ (وَهُوَ مَحْمَلُ الأَوَّلِ وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهِ أَنَّ الشَّرُطَ إِذَا كَانَ مُفِيدًا وَالْعَمَلُ بِهِ مُمْكِنًا وَجَبَ مُرَاعَاتُهُ وَالْمُخَالَفَةُ فِيهِ تُوجِبُ الصَّمَانَ ، وَإِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ مُفِيدًا أَوْ كَانَ وَلَمْ يُمْكِنُ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ كَمَا فِيمَا نَحْنُ فِيهِ يَلْغُو. (العناية: كتاب الوديعة، ح۸ ص ۴۹۴) وَلَوْ أَوْدَعَهُ وَدِيعَةً فَقَالَ: لَا تَدْفَعُهَا إِلَى امْرَأَتِك، أَوْ عَبْدِكَ، أَوْ وَلَدِكَ، أَوْ أجيرك، فَإِنِّى أَنَّهِمُهُمْ عَلَيْهَا، فَدَفَعَهَا إِلَى الَّذِي نَهَاهُ عَنْهُ، فَهَلَكَتْ: فَإِنْ كَانَ يَجِدُ بُدا مِنْ الدَّفْعِ إِلَيْهِ بِأَنْ كَانَ لَهُ سِوَاهُ أَهْلٌ وَخَدَمٌ فَهُوَ ضَامِنٌ، وَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يَجِدُ بُدًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ : لَمْ يَضْمَنُ، لِأَنَّ شَرْطَهُ هَذَا مُفِيدٌ، وَقَدْأْتَمِنُ الْإِنْسَانُ الرَّجُلَ عَلَى مَالِهِ وَلَا يَأْتَمِنُ زَوْجَتَهُ، إِلَّا أَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا يَلْزَمُهُ مُرَاعَاةُ شَرْطِهِ بِحَسَبِ الْإِمْكَانِ فَإِذَا كَانَ يَجِدُ بُدا مِنَ الدَّفع إلَى مَنْ نَهَاهُ عَنْهُ، فَهُوَ مُتَمَكِّنْ مِنْ حِفْظِهَا عَلَى الْوَجْهِ الْمَأْمُورِ بِهِ، فَيَصِيرُ ضَامِنَا بِحِفْظِهَا عَلَى الْوَجْهِ الْمَنْهِيِّ عَنْهُ، وَإِذَا كَانَ لَا يَجِدُ بُدًّا مِنْ ذَلِكَ، فَهُوَ حَافِظٌ لَهَا حَسَبَ الْإِمْكَانِ وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ أَكْثَرُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ : فَلَا يَضْمَنُهَا . (المبسوط للسرخسي كتاب الوديعة ، ج ۱۱ ص ۱۲۲)
Principles of Hidayah, Third. He cannot entrust the deposit to another without the owner's permission, because the owner trusts him, not another. (113) The condition: when it is not beneficial, or it is beneficial but acting upon it is not possible, it becomes void. Translation: The meaning of the above principle is that if the depositor places a condition that has no benefit, or it has benefit but acting upon it is not possible, then that condition is void; it is not necessary to observe it. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if the depositor said to the depositary: 'Do not give this deposit to your wife,' then the depositary gave it to his wife while he cannot protect it without giving it to his wife, there is no alternative, and the item became [؟] also, then the depositary is not liable. Similarly, if it was a quadruped and he stipulated not to give it to his slave, while he has no alternative except giving it to the slave, and he is the one who takes care of animals. Now the depositary placed a condition that is impossible to act upon, because a person by himself (for if he keeps it with others, meaning by leaving it in a house with the deposit and going out while there are others not his dependents, or entrusts it to others by moving it from his house and depositing it with others, he is liable, because the owner consented to his hand, not to another's, and hands differ in trustworthiness.) (al-'Inayah: Kitab al-Wadi'ah, vol. 8 p. 487) He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And if he keeps it with others, he is liable, i.e., with others than his dependents, because the owner did not consent to another's hand, and hands differ in trustworthiness, and because a thing does not guarantee its like, just as a mudarib does not enter into a mudarabah.) (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Kitab al-Wadi'ah, vol. 5 p. 77) Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Wadi'ah, vol. 3 p. 279. Principles of Hidayah, Third. He does not protect the deposit for twenty-four hours but rather keeps it with his wife, or animal care is usually done by servants. Now the wife and slave are not careless or negligent, so this is a condition that is impossible to act upon, and every condition that is impossible to act upon is void; hence the depositor's condition is also void. (And when the owner of the deposit says to the depositary: 'Do not hand it over to your wife,' and he hands it over to her, he is not liable. Its meaning: when he has no alternative to handing it over to her. This is known from the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir where he said: If he forbids him from giving it to any of his dependents, and he gives it to someone he cannot avoid, he is not liable. Similarly, if the deposit is a beast and he forbids him from giving it to his slave, or it is something that is kept on the hands of women and he forbids him from giving it to his wife. This is the meaning of his statement: (And it is the interpretation of the first, and the principle in it is that if the condition is beneficial and acting upon it is possible, observing it is obligatory, and violating it necessitates liability; and if it is not beneficial, or it is beneficial but acting upon it is not possible, as in our case, it is void.) (al-'Inayah: Kitab al-Wadi'ah, vol. 8 p. 494) And if someone deposits a deposit with him and says: 'Do not give it to your wife, or your slave, or your child, or your employee, for I suspect them regarding it,' and he gives it to the one he forbade, and it is lost: then if he has an alternative to giving it to him, i.e., he has other family and servants, then he is liable; and if he has no alternative, he is not liable, because his condition is beneficial, and a person entrusts a man with his property but does not entrust his wife. However, he is only obliged to observe his condition according to possibility. So if he has an alternative to giving it to the one he forbade, then he is able to keep it in the commanded manner, so he becomes liable by keeping it in the prohibited manner; and if he has no alternative, then he keeps it as much as possible, and he is not required to do more than that, so he is not liable. (al-Mabsut li al-Sarakhsi, Kitab al-Wadi'ah, vol. 11 p. 122)
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school concerning conditions in deposit (wadi'ah). The author states the principle: a condition that is either of no benefit (ghayr mufid) or beneficial but impossible to fulfill (la yumkin al-'amal bihi) is void (yalghu). He then applies this to the case where a depositor (mudi') instructs the depositary (muda') not to give the deposit to his wife or slave, but the depositary has no alternative—i.e., he cannot safeguard the item except by giving it to them. The passage clarifies that if the depositary has no other person to entrust the item to, he is not liable for loss despite violating the condition, because the condition is impossible to fulfill. The proofs cited are from al-'Inayah, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, al-Jami' al-Saghir, and al-Mabsut. The reasoning is that the owner's consent is specific to the depositary's hand, but when necessity dictates, the condition becomes void. The Hanafi position is that the depositary's liability depends on whether he had a feasible alternative. This aligns with the school's emphasis on possibility (imkan) in fulfilling conditions.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A stipulation or condition placed by the depositor regarding the handling of the deposit.
لغو (laghw): Void or null; a condition that is not legally effective.
ضامن (damin): Liable for compensation if the deposit is lost due to violation of a valid condition.
ودیعت (wadi'ah): A trust deposit; property left with someone for safekeeping.
مودع (mudi' / mudda'): The depositor (owner) or depositary (trustee); context determines which.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle in this passage, when is a depositary (muda') not liable for giving the deposit to his wife despite being prohibited?
A) When the wife is trustworthy.
B) When the depositary has no alternative to protect the deposit except by giving it to his wife.
C) When the depositary forgets the condition.
D) When the owner gives permission after the fact.

Key Takeaway
A condition that is impossible to fulfill is void (laghw) in a deposit contract, so the depositary is not liable for violating it.

Impossible Conditions in Deposit: Void and No Liability
Explaining when a depositary's violation of a condition does not incur liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a condition in a deposit is void if impossible to perform, and determine whether the depositary is liable based on availability of alternatives.

Core Idea
A condition in deposit is void if impossible; no liability for violating it when no alternative exists.

This lesson examines a key principle in Hanafi fiqh regarding conditions in deposit contracts (wadi'ah). The depositor may impose conditions, but not all are binding. When a condition is impossible to fulfill—for example, forbidding the depositary to entrust the deposit to his own wife when he has no one else—the condition becomes void and violating it does not incur liability. You will learn the criteria that make a condition binding and how necessity affects liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
Determine what act the depositary performed (e.g., handing the deposit to his wife) and what condition the depositor imposed (e.g., not to give it to his wife). Note that the condition is part of the deposit contract.
The condition must be explicitly stated by the depositor.
2
Assess the condition's feasibility
Ask: Is the condition beneficial (mufid) and possible to perform (mumkin al-'amal)? A condition is beneficial if it serves a legitimate purpose, such as protecting the deposit from suspected persons. If the condition is impossible—because the depositary has no alternative caretaker—then it is not binding.
Impossibility here refers to practical inability, not theoretical.
3
Determine the presence of alternatives
Check whether the depositary had other trustworthy persons (e.g., other family members, servants) to whom he could entrust the deposit. If alternatives exist, he must obey the condition; if not, the condition is void and he may act as needed.
The ruling in al-Jami' al-Saghir distinguishes based on the existence of a 'bud' (alternative).
4
Apply the liability rule
If the depositary violated a beneficial and possible condition without necessity, he is liable (damin) for any loss. If the condition was impossible or he had no alternative, he is not liable because he preserved the deposit to the best of his ability.
This follows the principle: 'al-shart idha kana mufidan wa al-amal bihi mumkinan wajab... wa idha lam yakun mufidan aw lam yumkin al-amal bihi yalghu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول بدایہ ثالث چوبیس گھنٹہ ودیعت کی حفاظت نہیں کرتا بلکہ اپنی بیوی کے پاس رکھتا ہے، یا جانوروں کی دیکھے بال عموماً نوکر چاکر کرتے ہیں۔ اب بیوی اور غلام لا پرواہ اور غافل بھی نہیں، تو یہ ایسی شرط ہے جس پر عمل ممکن نہیں اور ہر ایسی شرط جس پر عمل کرنا ممکن نہ ہو وہ لغو ہوتی ہے، لہذا مورع کی یہ شرط بھی لغو ہوگی۔
(وَإِذَا قَالَ صَاحِبُ الْوَدِيعَةِ لِلْمُودَعِ لَا تُسَلِّمُهَا إِلَى زَوْجَتِكَ فَسَلَّمَهَا إِلَيْهَا لَا يَضْمَنُ مَعْنَاهُ: إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مِنَ التَّسْلِيمِ إِلَيْهَا بُدٌ، عُلِمَ ذَلِكَ مِنْ رِوَايَةِ الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ حَيْثُ قَالَ إِذَا نَهَاهُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَهَا إِلَى أَحَدٍ مِنْ عِيَالِهِ فَدَفَعَهَا إِلَى مَنْ لَا بُدَّ لَهُ مِنْهُ لَا يَضْمَنُ، كَمَا إِذَا كَانَتِ الْوَدِيعَةُ دَابَّةً فَنَهَاهُ عَنِ الدَّفْعِ إِلَى غُلَامِهِ، أَوْ كَانَتْ شَيْئًا يُحْفَظُ عَلَى أَيْدِي النِّسَاءِ فَنَهَاهُ عَنِ الدَّفْعِ إِلَى امْرَأَتِهِ وَهَذَا مَعْنَى قَوْلِهِ (وَهُوَ مَحْمَلُ الأَوَّلِ وَالأَصْلُ فِيهِ أَنَّ الشَّرْطَ إِذَا كَانَ مُفِيدًا وَالْعَمَلُ بِهِ مُمْكِنًا وَجَبَ مُرَاعَاتُهُ وَالمُخَالَفَةُ فِيهِ تُوجِبُ الضَّمَانَ، وَإِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ مُفِيدًا أَوْ كَانَ وَلَمْ يُمْكِنِ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ كَمَا فِيمَا نَحْنُ فِيهِ يَلْغُو. (العناية: كتاب الوديعة، ح۸ ص ۴۹۴) وَلَوْ أَوْدَعَهُ وَدِيعَةً فَقَالَ: لَا تَدْفَعْهَا إِلَى امْرَأَتِكَ، أَوْ عَبْدِكَ، أَوْ وَلَدِكَ، أَوْ أَجِيرِكَ، فَإِنِّي أَتَّهِمُهُمْ عَلَيْهَا، فَدَفَعَهَا إِلَى الَّذِي نَهَاهُ عَنْهُ، فَهَلَكَتْ: فَإِنْ كَانَ يَجِدُ بُدًا مِنَ الدَّفْعِ إِلَيْهِ بِأَنْ كَانَ لَهُ سِوَاهُ أَهْلٌ وَخَدَمٌ فَهُوَ ضَامِنٌ، وَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يَجِدُ بُدًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ : لَمْ يَضْمَنُ، لِأَنَّ شَرْطَهُ هَذَا مُفِيدٌ، وَقَدْ يَأْتَمِنُ الْإِنْسَانُ الرَّجُلَ عَلَى مَالِهِ وَلَا يَأْتَمِنُ زَوْجَتَهُ، إِلَّا أَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا يَلْزَمُهُ مُرَاعَاةُ شَرْطِهِ بِحَسَبِ الْإِمْكَانِ فَإِذَا كَانَ يَجِدُ بُدًا مِنَ الدَّفْعِ إِلَى مَنْ نَهَاهُ عَنْهُ، فَهُوَ مُتَمَكِّنٌ مِنْ حِفْظِهَا عَلَى الْوَجْهِ الْمَأْمُورِ بِهِ، فَيَصِيرُ ضَامِنًا بِحِفْظِهَا عَلَى الْوَجْهِ الْمَنْهِيِّ عَنْهُ، وَإِذَا كَانَ لَا يَجِدُ بُدًّا مِنْ ذَلِكَ، فَهُوَ حَافِظٌ لَهَا حَسَبَ الْإِمْكَانِ وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ أَكْثَرُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ : فَلَا يَضْمَنُهَا . (المبسوط للسرخسي كتاب الوديعة، ج ۱۱ ص ۱۲۲)
The person entrusted with the deposit does not guard it for twenty-four hours but keeps it with his wife, or animals are generally looked after by servants. If the wife and servant are not negligent and careless, then such a condition is one upon which action is not possible, and every condition upon which action is not possible is void. Therefore, the condition of the depositor is also void. (And if the owner of the deposit says to the depositary: Do not hand it over to your wife, and he hands it over to her, he is not liable. Meaning: if he had no alternative to handing it over to her. This is known from the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir where he said: If he forbade him from giving it to any of his dependents, and he gave it to one from whom he had no alternative, he is not liable. Just as if the deposit was an animal and he forbade him from giving it to his servant, or it was something that is preserved by women and he forbade him from giving it to his wife. And this is the meaning of his statement: And it is the interpretation of the first, and the principle is that when a condition is beneficial and action upon it is possible, it must be observed, and violating it incurs liability. And when it is not beneficial, or it is beneficial but action upon it is not possible, as in our case, it is void. (al-`Inayah, Kitab al-Wadi`ah, vol. 8, p. 494) And if he deposited with him a deposit and said: Do not give it to your wife, or your slave, or your child, or your employee, for I suspect them of it, and he gave it to the one he forbade, and it perished: then if he finds an alternative to giving it to that person, in that he has other family and servants other than him, then he is liable. And if he finds no alternative to that, he is not liable, because his condition is beneficial, and a person trusts a man with his wealth and does not trust his wife. However, he is obliged to observe his condition according to possibility. So if he finds an alternative to giving it to the one he forbade, then he is able to preserve it in the commanded manner, so he becomes liable by preserving it in the forbidden manner. And if he finds no alternative to that, then he preserves it according to possibility and nothing more is required of him, so he is not liable for it. (al-Mabsut li al-Sarakhsi, Kitab al-Wadi`ah, vol. 11, p. 122)
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the validity of conditions in deposit (wadi'ah). The author explains that a condition placed by the depositor (muudi') on the depositary (muda') is binding only if it is both beneficial and possible to fulfill. If the condition is impossible to perform—as in the example where the depositor forbids the depositary to entrust the deposit to his own wife when the depositary has no one else to guard it—the condition is considered void (laghw) and the depositary is not liable (daman) if he violates it out of necessity. The proof is drawn from the ruling in al-Jami' al-Saghir: if the depositor forbids handing the deposit to any dependent but the depositary must do so, there is no liability. The principle (asl) is that a beneficial and possible condition must be observed; violation incurs liability. But if impossible, the condition is void. The same ruling applies when the depositor specifically forbids handing to wife, slave, child, or employee: if the depositary has an alternative (other trustworthy persons), he is liable for violating the condition; otherwise, he is not. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Key Terms
وَدِيعَة (wadi'ah): A deposit; a contract of bailment where property is entrusted to another for safekeeping without compensation.
شَرْط (shart): A condition imposed by the depositor on the depositary regarding the handling of the deposit.
ضَامِن (damin): Liable for compensation (daman) if the deposit is lost due to violation of a valid condition.
بُدّ (budd): Alternative; the existence of other trustworthy persons to whom the deposit could be entrusted.
لَغْو (laghw): Void; legally ineffective. A condition that is laghw has no effect and need not be observed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The depositary is liable because he violated the condition.
B) The depositary is not liable because he had no alternative; the condition is void.
C) The condition is automatically void regardless of circumstances.
D) The depositary must still obey and find another way.

Key Takeaway
A condition in a deposit is void if impossible to fulfill; the depositary is not liable for loss if he had no alternative to violating the condition.

The Principle That a Thing Does Not Include What Is Above It
Explaining a legal maxim and its application to loans and leases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a borrower becomes liable if he leases the borrowed item and explain why using the principle that a non-compensatory contract cannot encompass a compensatory contract.

Core Idea
A borrower cannot lease the borrowed item because 'Aariyah (loan) is weaker than Ijarah (lease).

This lesson examines a key Hanafi legal maxim: 'al-shay'u la yatadammunu ma huwa fawqahu' (a thing does not include what is above it). We will see how this principle operates in the context of borrowed goods to determine the borrower's liability when he exceeds his authority by leasing the item.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Locate the maxim 'al-shay'u la yatadammunu ma huwa fawqahu' in the Arabic text. Understand its literal meaning: a lesser thing cannot contain a greater thing.
This principle is a rational (aqli) proof.
2
Classify the Contracts
Distinguish between 'Aariyah (non-compensatory loan) and Ijarah (compensatory lease). Recognize that Ijarah is 'above' 'Aariyah in strength because it involves consideration.
Ijarah is a contract of exchange ('aqd mu'awadah), while 'Aariyah is a gratuitous contract.
3
Apply the Principle
Apply the maxim: since 'Aariyah is lesser, it cannot grant the authority to perform Ijarah, which is greater. Therefore, the borrower (musta'ir) has no right to lease the item.
The borrower's possession is limited to personal use.
4
Derive the Legal Consequence
If the borrower leases the item and it is destroyed, he becomes liable (damin) because he acted beyond the scope of the loan contract.
Liability arises due to unauthorized use leading to loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اَلشَّيْءُ لَا يَتَضَمَّنُ مَا هُوَ فَوْقَهُ. ترجمہ: شے اپنے سے مافوق کو متضمن نہیں ہوتی ۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کمتر شے اپنے سے زیادہ قوت والی چیز کو اپنے ضمن میں نہیں لے سکتی ، لہذا عقد غیر معاوضہ عقد معاوضہ کو تضمن نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ عقد معاوضہ قومی اور بڑھ کر ہے عقدِ غیر معاوضہ سے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ مستعغیر یعنی عاریت پر لینے والے کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ وہ شے مستعار کو آگے کرایہ پر دے دے، کیونکہ اعارہ اجارہ سے کم درجہ کا ہے اور شے اپنے مافوق کو تضمن نہیں ہوتی لہذا اعارہ بھی اجارہ کو تضمن نہ ہوگا، اس لیے اگر مسیر نے نے مستعار کو اجارہ پر دیا اور وہ ہلاک ہوگئی تو مستعیر ضامن ہوگا۔
The thing does not include what is above it. Translation: A thing does not encompass what is above it. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that a lesser thing cannot incorporate a stronger thing within itself, therefore a non-compensatory contract cannot encompass a compensatory contract, because a compensatory contract is stronger and higher than a non-compensatory contract. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that the borrower (musta'ir) does not have the permission to lease the borrowed item, because 'Aariyah (loan) is of a lower degree than Ijarah (lease), and a thing does not encompass what is above it. Therefore, if the borrower gave the borrowed item on lease and it was destroyed, the borrower becomes liable.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents a legal principle and its application. It begins by stating the principle 'al-shay'u la yatadammunu ma huwa fawqahu' (a thing does not include what is above it). The commentator explains that a lesser contract cannot contain a greater contract. Specifically, a non-compensatory contract (like 'Aariyah) cannot include a compensatory contract (like Ijarah) because the latter is stronger. This principle is then applied to the case of a borrower (musta'ir): he cannot lease the borrowed item because 'Aariyah is less than Ijarah. If he does lease it and the item is destroyed, he becomes liable (daman). The ruling is taken from al-Hidayah. The principle is a legal maxim used in Hanafi fiqh to determine the scope of contracts.

Key Terms
عَارِيَة ('Aariyah): Loan of a chattel for use without compensation.
إِجَارَة (Ijarah): Lease or hire contract, a compensatory transfer of usufruct.
ضَامِن (Damin): Liable or guarantor, responsible for compensation in case of loss.
مُسْتَعِير (Musta'ir): Borrower, the one who receives an 'Aariyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'al-shay'u la yatadammunu ma huwa fawqahu', what happens if a borrower (musta'ir) leases the borrowed item and it is destroyed?
A) The borrower is not liable because he had permission to use.
B) The borrower is liable (daman) because 'Aariyah cannot include Ijarah.
C) The owner is liable because the borrower acted without authorization.
D) The borrower is only liable if he received compensation for the lease.

Key Takeaway
A borrower cannot lease a borrowed item because the loan contract (non-compensatory) cannot authorize a lease contract (compensatory); if he does and the item is lost, he is liable.

‘Aariyah as Tamleek: Permissibility of Sub-Lending
Establishing that 'Aariyah is tamleek, allowing the borrower to sub-lend

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'Aariyah and apply the ruling that the borrower may sub-lend items that do not vary with use, using qiyas on the case of wasiyyah for service.

Core Idea
A loan ('Aariyah) in the Hanafi school transfers ownership of usufruct, so the borrower can sub-lend it like any owner.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies the Hanafi definition of 'Aariyah: it is not mere permission (ibahah) but transfer of ownership of the usufruct (tamleek al-manafi'). This definition directly impacts whether the borrower can lend the item to a third party. The author provides a qiyas (analogy) with a bequest of a slave's service to prove this.

Guided Path
1
State the two competing definitions
Identify the Hanafi definition (tamleek al-manafi') and the Shafi'i definition (ibahah al-intifa').
This distinction is the foundation of the entire ruling.
2
Recognise the consequence of tamleek
If the borrower owns the usufruct, he can transfer it to another, just like any owner. This permits sub-lending.
The condition is that the item must not change or vary with different users.
3
Analyse the qiyas proof
The case of a wasiyyah for a slave's service: the beneficiary may lend the slave's service because he owns that usufruct. Analogously, the borrower of an item owns its usufruct.
The illa is tamleek al-manafi'.
4
Note the condition for sub-lending
Permitted only for items that do not differ with different users (e.g., land, houses, beasts of burden). Excluded are items like clothing that vary with the user.
If the condition is violated, the borrower becomes a guarantor if the item is damaged.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school considers 'Aariyah as ibahah, so the borrower cannot sub-lend without the owner's permission. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The practical difference turns on the definition of the contract.

Source Text

(١١) اَلْعَارِيَةُ تَمُلِيْكُ الْمَنَافِع عِنْدَنَا . ترجمہ ہمارے نزدیک عاریت منافع کی تملیک کا نام ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک عاریت إِبَاحَةُ الْاِنْتِفَاعِ بِمُلِكُ الْغَيْرِ “ کا نام نہیں ہے، یعنی عاریت تملیک المنافع بلاعوض کا نام ہے۔ الهداية كتاب الوديعة، ح ۳ ص ۲۸۳ قَالَ (وَلَيْسَ لِلْمُسْتَعِيرِ أَنْ يُوَاجِرَ مَا اسْتَعَارَهُ إِلَخُ وَلَيْسَ لِلْمُسْتَعِيرِ أَنْ يُؤَاجِرَ الْمُسْتَعَارَ، فَإِنْ آجَرَهُ، فَعَطِبَ ضَمِنَ لِوَجْهَيْنِ: أَحَدُهُمَا أَنَّ الْإِعَارَةَ دُونَ الْإِجَارَةِ الشَّيءُ لَا يَتَضَمَّنُ مَا هُوَ فَوْقَه. (العناية: كتاب العارية، ج ۹ ص ۹) وليس للمستعير أن يؤاجر ما استعاره، ولا أن يرهنه لأن الشيء لا يتضمن ما فوقه. اللباب فى شرح الكتاب: كتاب العارية، ج ۲ ص ۲۰۲ الهداية كتاب الوديعة، ج ۳ ص ۲۸۳ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ مستعیر شے مستعار کو آگے عاریت پر دے سکتا ہے، بشرطیکہ وہ چیز استعمال سے بدلتی نہ ہو اور مختلف بھی نہ ہوتی ہو، مثلاً جانور پر بوجھ لادنا، زمین میں کاشت کرنا ، مکان میں سکونت اپنانا وغیرہ، کیونکہ عاریت تملیک منافع کا نام ہے اور تملیک میں متملک آگے مالک بنا سکتا ہے، جیسے کہ اگر کسی نے کسی کے لیے اپنے غلام کی خدمت کی وصیت کی تو موصی لہ بالخدمت اس غلام کو دوسرے کی خدمت کے لیے دے سکتا ہے، کیونکہ یہ منافع کی تملیک ہے، بالکل ایسے ہی عاریت میں بھی مستعبیر آگے تملیک منافع یعنی منافع کا مالک بنا سکتا ہے۔ وَلَنَا أَنَّهَا تَمُلِيكُ الْمَنَافِعِ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ فَيَتَضَمَّنُ مِثْلَهُ كَالْمُوصَى لَهُ بِالْخِدْمَةِ جَازَ أَنْ يُعِيرَ لِتَمَلْكِهِ الْمَنْفَعَةَ. (العناية: كتاب العارية، ج ۹ ص ١٠) (قَوْلُهُ: وَلَهُ أَنْ يُعِيرَهُ إِذَا كَانَ مِمَّا لَا يَخْتَلِفُ بِاخْتِلَافِ الْمُسْتَعْمِلِ) قَالَ عَامَّةُ الشَّرَّاحِ كَالْحَمْلِ وَالاسْتِخْدَامِ وَالسُّكْنَى وَالزَّرَاعَةِ. (فتح القدير : كتاب العارية، ج ۹ ص ١٠) (وله) أى لـلـمـعير (أن يعيره إذا كان مما لا يختلف باختلاف المستعمل)..... ونحن نقول هو تملیک المنافع على ما ذکرنا یعنی فی هذا الباب فیملک الإعارة) يعني إذا كانت الإعارة تمليكا للمنافع يملك المستعير حينئذ الإعارة، لأن الشيء يتضمن مثله ( كالموصى له بالخدمة) أى بخدمة عبد مثلا يجوز له أن يعيره لتملك المنفعة. (البناية: كتاب العارية، ج ۱۰ ص ۱۴۸ ) الهداية كتاب الهبة، ج ۳ ص ٢٨٤
(11) According to us, 'Aariyah is transfer of ownership of usufruct. Translation: According to us, 'Aariyah is the name for transfer of ownership of usufruct. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that according to us, 'Aariyah is not the name for 'permission to use another's property', rather 'Aariyah is the name for transfer of ownership of usufruct without compensation. ... The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that the borrower can give the borrowed item on 'Aariyah (lend it to another), provided that the item does not change with use and does not vary (with different users), for example, loading an animal, cultivating land, residing in a house, etc. Because 'Aariyah is tamleek al-manafi' (transfer of ownership of usufruct), and in tamleek, the owner can make another owner. Similar to the case of a person who makes a wasiyyah for the service of his slave to someone, that person can give the slave to another for service, because it is tamleek of usufruct. Similarly, in 'Aariyah, the borrower can transfer ownership of usufruct to another. Our proof is that it is tamleek al-manafi' as we said, so it includes its like, like the one who is bequeathed service can lend (the slave) because he owns the usufruct. ... (His saying: and he may lend it if it does not differ with the difference of users) the general commentators said: like carrying, employing, dwelling, and cultivating. ... (And he, i.e., the borrower, may lend it if it does not differ with difference of users)... and we say it is tamleek al-manafi' as we mentioned in this chapter, so he owns the 'Aariyah, meaning if 'Aariyah is tamleek of usufruct, then the borrower owns the 'Aariyah (i.e., can sub-lend) because a thing includes its like, like the one who is bequeathed service, it is permissible for him to lend it due to his ownership of the usufruct.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi definition of 'Aariyah as tamleek al-manafi' (transfer of ownership of usufruct) rather than mere ibahah al-intifa' (permission to use). This definition has practical implications: the borrower (musta'ir) can sub-lend the borrowed item to a third party, because he owns the usufruct and can transfer it. However, this is conditional: the item must not change or vary with different users (e.g., animals for loading, land for cultivation, house for dwelling). The proof is analogy (qiyas) with the case of a wasiyyah for service: if someone is bequeathed the service of a slave, he can lend the slave to another for service, as he owns that usufruct. The passage cites several commentaries: al-'Inayah, Fath al-Qadir, and al-Binayah, all reinforcing this view. The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
تَمْلِيْكُ الْمَنَافِع (Tamleek al-manafi'): Transfer of ownership of the usufruct, as opposed to mere permission to use.
إِبَاحَةُ الْاِنْتِفَاعِ (Ibahah al-intifa'): Permission to use, without transfer of ownership.
مُسْتَعِير (Musta'ir): Borrower, the person who receives something on 'Aariyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The borrower may lend it freely for any purpose.
B) The borrower may lend it only if the item does not change or vary with different users.
C) The borrower may lend it only after obtaining the owner's permission.
D) The borrower may never lend it because 'Aariyah is only permission.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'Aariyah as tamleek al-manafi' allows the borrower to sub-lend items that do not vary with use, based on qiyas with a bequest of service.
